[ASSISTANT]
That file is **not a Windows executable**. It’s a **Linux 64-bit ELF binary** that was just named `.exe`, so Windows won’t run it natively.

### Option A (fastest): run it on Windows via WSL2
1) Install WSL (Windows 11 / recent Windows 10):
- Open PowerShell **as Administrator** and run:
```powershell
wsl --install
```
Reboot if it asks.

2) Put the file somewhere like `C:\temp\PlastiPak_LineClearance.exe`

3) Open **Ubuntu** (or whatever WSL distro you installed) and run:
```bash
cd /mnt/c/temp
cp PlastiPak_LineClearance.exe ~/PlastiPak_LineClearance
chmod +x ~/PlastiPak_LineClearance
~/PlastiPak_LineClearance
```

### Option B (native Windows app): you need a Windows build
There’s no reliable “convert this Linux binary into a Windows .exe” trick. You need:
- the **source code** to compile for Windows, **or**
- whoever produced it to provide a **Windows build**.

If you tell me what it was built with (C/C++/Go/Rust/Python/.NET/etc.) or share the repo/source, I’ll give you the exact Windows build steps.

[ASSISTANT]
That error means this isn’t a “normal Linux GUI app.” It’s a **PyInstaller** binary, and it was packaged **without Tkinter included**. So the embedded Python inside the executable can’t import `tkinter`, and it will crash **everywhere**, not just in WSL.

Installing `python3-tk` in WSL usually **won’t fix a PyInstaller onefile** build, because it doesn’t use your system Python’s stdlib/modules.

## What will fix it (real fixes)

### 1) Rebuild the app correctly (best)
You need the **source** (or whoever made it needs to rebuild it) with Tkinter properly bundled.

**On Windows (to produce a real Windows .exe):**
```powershell
py -m pip install --upgrade pip pyinstaller
py -m PyInstaller --onefile --windowed app.py --collect-all tkinter
```

If they’re using a `.spec` file, the equivalent is “collect tkinter + tcl/tk data” (PyInstaller’s hooks usually handle this when tkinter exists at build time).

**Important:** the builder must have a Python install that actually includes Tk/Tcl (standard python.org installer does).

### 2) Run from source with system Python (stopgap, no packaging)
If you can get `app.py` and whatever other `.py` files it needs, then you can run it directly:

**WSL (Ubuntu/Debian):**
```bash
sudo apt update
sudo apt install -y python3 python3-tk
python3 app.py
```

**Windows:**
Install Python from python.org (it includes Tkinter), then:
```powershell
py app.py
```

## Bottom line
You can’t “make this run on Windows” from this binary as-is. It’s a Linux PyInstaller build that’s missing Tkinter. You need either:
- a **proper Windows build**, or
- the **source** to run/rebuild.

If you can share `app.py` (or the project folder / repo), I’ll give you an exact Windows build command that produces a working `.exe` and includes every dependency.

[ASSISTANT]
Your program is a **Tkinter GUI** (`import tkinter as tk`) and it’s crashing because the packaged binary you ran was missing Tkinter. Running it on **Windows** is straightforward if you run from source (or rebuild a proper Windows `.exe`). fileciteturn0file1L1-L9

## Run it on Windows (no EXE build yet)

1) Put `app.py` in a folder, e.g. `C:\PlastiPak\app.py` (same folder is fine for `parser.py` too, but `app.py` already contains the parser). fileciteturn0file1L34-L92 fileciteturn0file0L1-L45

2) Install Python on Windows (python.org installer). During install, check:
- **Add Python to PATH**
- **tcl/tk and IDLE** (this is what provides Tkinter)

3) Open PowerShell in that folder and install dependencies:
```powershell
cd C:\PlastiPak
py -m pip install --upgrade pip
py -m pip install pandas
```
(Your code uses `pandas` for the DataFrame work.) fileciteturn0file1L1-L6

4) Run:
```powershell
py app.py
```

If it opens a window titled **“Plasti-Pak Line Clearance Optimizer”**, you’re done. fileciteturn0file1L11-L18

---

## Build a real Windows `.exe` (so you don’t need Python installed)

From the same folder:

```powershell
py -m pip install pyinstaller
py -m PyInstaller --onefile --windowed --clean --noconfirm app.py
```

Your EXE will land in:
- `dist\app.exe`

If Tkinter still fails in the EXE (rare on Windows if Python is installed correctly), build with explicit collection:
```powershell
py -m PyInstaller --onefile --windowed --clean --noconfirm --collect-all tkinter app.py
```

---

## Notes (so you don’t chase ghosts)
- `app.py` **does not import `parser.py`**; it has its own `parse_sap_xml()` already, so `parser.py` isn’t required for the GUI to run. fileciteturn0file1L34-L92 fileciteturn0file0L1-L45
- The failure you saw in WSL (`ModuleNotFoundError: tkinter`) is exactly what happens when Tk/Tcl isn’t available or wasn’t bundled into the PyInstaller build. fileciteturn0file1L1-L9

If you tell me what version of Windows you’re on (10/11) and which Python you installed (python.org vs Microsoft Store), I’ll give you the most reliable install path for Tkinter on that setup.

## 1) Install real Python (not the Store stub)

## 2) Verify Python is actually there
In PowerShell:

At least one of those should work. If neither works, Python didn’t get added to PATH / py launcher not installed.

In the folder with `app.py`:

```powershell
cd C:\temp

py -m PyInstaller --onefile --windowed --clean --noconfirm app.py
```
Your EXE will be:
```text
C:\temp\dist\app.exe
```

## If Windows keeps trying to send you to the Microsoft Store
That message means Windows has an “app execution alias” for python but no python installed.

Fix it:
**Settings → Apps → Advanced app settings → App execution aliases**
- toggle OFF **python.exe**
- toggle OFF **python3.exe**

Then reopen PowerShell and re-run:
```powershell
python --version
py --version
```

## If you want, I can give you a one-command installer path
If you’re okay using **winget** (built into Windows), run:
```powershell
winget install -e --id Python.Python.3.12
```
Then reopen PowerShell and continue with the commands above.

You’re in a Linux shell as **root** (`[root@ElinVoss …]`), but it’s **not Debian/Ubuntu** (no `apt`, no `sudo`). Also, there’s **no Python installed** (`python3: command not found`). And even if you install Python, your **PyInstaller binary will still fail** because it was built missing Tkinter.

So you have two separate paths:

## Path 1 (recommended): build a real Windows EXE on Windows
On Windows you currently have no Python installed, so fix that first:

```powershell
winget install -e --id Python.Python.3.12
```

Close PowerShell, open it again, then:

```powershell
cd C:\temp

python -m PyInstaller --onefile --windowed --clean --noconfirm app.py
```

Result: `C:\temp\dist\app.exe`

(Using `python` instead of `py` avoids the launcher dependency.)

---

## Path 2: run from source on your Linux box (needs the right package manager)
Since this isn’t apt-based, use the correct installer **for your distro**:

### If it’s RHEL/CentOS/Fedora (common with `[root@host]`)
Try:
```bash
dnf --version || yum --version
```

Then install:
- Fedora/RHEL9+:
```bash
dnf install -y python3 python3-tkinter python3-pip
```
- CentOS/RHEL7/8:
```bash
yum install -y python3 python3-tkinter python3-pip
```

Run:
```bash
cd /mnt/c/temp
python3 -m pip install --upgrade pip pandas
python3 app.py
```

### If it’s Alpine Linux
```bash
apk add --no-cache python3 py3-pip tk tcl
cd /mnt/c/temp
python3 -m pip install --upgrade pip pandas
python3 app.py
```

### If it’s Arch
```bash
pacman -Syu --noconfirm python python-pip tk
cd /mnt/c/temp
python -m pip install --upgrade pip pandas
python app.py
```

---

## One important gotcha
If this Linux environment is **WSL without GUI support**, Tkinter windows won’t display unless you have:
- **WSLg** (Windows 11) enabled, or
- an X server on Windows (VcXsrv/Xming) and `DISPLAY` configured.

That’s why the Windows-native build is the cleanest.

That tells me whether you need `dnf`, `yum`, `apk`, or `pacman`, and I’ll give you the exact install line for Python+Tkinter for *your* system.

import xml.etree.ElementTree as ET, pandas as pd, re, math, os
def parse_sap_xml(file_path):
    tree = ET.parse(file_path)
    root = tree.getroot()
    ns = {'ss': 'urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet'}
    data_rows=[]
    for row in root.findall('.//ss:Row', ns):
        for cell in row.findall('ss:Cell', ns):
            data_node = cell.find('ss:Data', ns)
            if data_node is not None and data_node.text:
                lines = data_node.text.split('\n')
                for line in lines:
                    if line.startswith('|') and 'StorageBin' not in line and '---' not in line:
                        parts=[p.strip() for p in line.split('|')]
                        if len(parts)>11:
                            try:
                                bin_name=parts[6]
                                material=parts[7]
                                desc=parts[8]
                                total_stock=float(parts[11].replace(',','')) if parts[11] else 0.0
                                cap=float(parts[17].replace(',','')) if len(parts)>17 and parts[17] else 0.0
                                data_rows.append({"Bin":bin_name,"Material":material,"Description":desc,"TotalStock":total_stock,"Capacity":cap})
                            except Exception:
                                continue
    return pd.DataFrame(data_rows)

df=parse_sap_xml("/mnt/data/bins.xml")
df.shape, df.head(3).to_dict(orient="records")

import pandas as pd, re, math
df2=df.copy()
def normalize_bin(b):
    m=re.match(r'^\d+([A-Z]\d+)$', str(b).strip())
    return m.group(1) if m else str(b).strip()
df2["BinNorm"]=df2["Bin"].apply(normalize_bin)
# filter A02-G47
pat=re.compile(r'^([A-G])(0[2-9]|[1-3][0-9]|4[0-7])$')
df_f=df2[df2["BinNorm"].apply(lambda x: bool(pat.match(x)))].copy()
df_f.shape, df_f["Bin"].head(), df_f["BinNorm"].head()

df_f["Row"]=df_f["BinNorm"].str[0]
df_f["Num"]=df_f["BinNorm"].str[1:].astype(int)

moves=[]
for material, group in df_f.groupby("Material"):
    if len(group)<2: 
        continue
    sources=group[group["TotalStock"]>0].sort_values(by="Num", ascending=False).copy()
    targets=group.sort_values(by="Num", ascending=True).copy()
    # We'll operate on a copy of target stocks in targets dataframe
    for s_idx, s_row in sources.iterrows():
        source_bin=s_row["BinNorm"]
        source_num=s_row["Num"]
        source_stock=float(s_row["TotalStock"])
        # iterate targets
        for t_idx, t_row in targets.iterrows():
            target_bin=t_row["BinNorm"]
            target_num=int(t_row["Num"])
            if target_num >= source_num:
                continue
            target_cap=float(t_row["Capacity"])
            target_stock=float(targets.at[t_idx,"TotalStock"])
            if target_stock >= target_cap:
                continue
            space=target_cap-target_stock
            move_qty=min(source_stock, space)
            if move_qty>0:
                moves.append({
                    "Material": material,
                    "Desc": s_row["Description"],
                    "From": source_bin,
                    "To": target_bin,
                    "Qty": move_qty
                })
                source_stock -= move_qty
                targets.at[t_idx,"TotalStock"]=target_stock+move_qty
            if source_stock<=0:
                break
len(moves), moves[:5]

def compute_moves(df, same_row=False):
    pat=re.compile(r'^([A-G])(0[2-9]|[1-3][0-9]|4[0-7])$')
    df=df.copy()
    df["BinNorm"]=df["Bin"].apply(lambda b: re.match(r'^\d+([A-Z]\d+)$', str(b).strip()).group(1) if re.match(r'^\d+([A-Z]\d+)$', str(b).strip()) else str(b).strip())
    df=df[df["BinNorm"].apply(lambda x: bool(pat.match(x)))].copy()
    df["Row"]=df["BinNorm"].str[0]
    df["Num"]=df["BinNorm"].str[1:].astype(int)
    moves=[]
    for material, group in df.groupby("Material"):
        if len(group)<2: 
            continue
        sources=group[group["TotalStock"]>0].sort_values(by="Num", ascending=False).copy()
        targets=group.sort_values(by="Num", ascending=True).copy()
        for s_idx, s_row in sources.iterrows():
            source_bin=s_row["BinNorm"]
            source_num=int(s_row["Num"])
            source_row=s_row["Row"]
            source_stock=float(s_row["TotalStock"])
            for t_idx, t_row in targets.iterrows():
                target_bin=t_row["BinNorm"]
                target_num=int(t_row["Num"])
                if target_num >= source_num:
                    continue
                if same_row and t_row["Row"] != source_row:
                    continue
                target_cap=float(t_row["Capacity"])
                target_stock=float(targets.at[t_idx,"TotalStock"])
                if target_stock >= target_cap:
                    continue
                space=target_cap-target_stock
                move_qty=min(source_stock, space)
                if move_qty>0:
                    moves.append({
                        "Material": material,
                        "Description": s_row["Description"],
                        "From": source_bin,
                        "To": target_bin,
                        "Qty": move_qty
                    })
                    source_stock -= move_qty
                    targets.at[t_idx,"TotalStock"]=target_stock+move_qty
                if source_stock<=0:
                    break
    return pd.DataFrame(moves)

moves_any=compute_moves(df2, same_row=False)
moves_row=compute_moves(df2, same_row=True)

import pandas as pd, re, xml.etree.ElementTree as ET, os

def parse_sap_xml(file_path):
    tree = ET.parse(file_path)
    root = tree.getroot()
    ns = {'ss': 'urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet'}
    data_rows=[]
    for row in root.findall('.//ss:Row', ns):
        for cell in row.findall('ss:Cell', ns):
            data_node = cell.find('ss:Data', ns)
            if data_node is not None and data_node.text:
                lines = data_node.text.split('\n')
                for line in lines:
                    if line.startswith('|') and 'StorageBin' not in line and '---' not in line:
                        parts=[p.strip() for p in line.split('|')]
                        if len(parts)>11:
                            try:
                                bin_name=parts[6]
                                material=parts[7]
                                desc=parts[8]
                                total_stock=float(parts[11].replace(',','')) if parts[11] else 0.0
                                cap=float(parts[17].replace(',','')) if len(parts)>17 and parts[17] else 0.0
                                data_rows.append({"BinRaw":bin_name,"Material":material,"Description":desc,"TotalStock":total_stock,"Capacity":cap})
                            except Exception:
                                continue
    return pd.DataFrame(data_rows)

def normalize_bin(b):
    b=str(b).strip()
    m=re.match(r'^\d+([A-Z]\d+)$', b)
    return m.group(1) if m else b

def compute_moves(df, same_row=False):
    pat=re.compile(r'^([A-G])(0[2-9]|[1-3][0-9]|4[0-7])$')
    df=df.copy()
    df["Bin"]=df["BinRaw"].apply(normalize_bin)
    df=df[df["Bin"].apply(lambda x: bool(pat.match(x)))].copy()
    df["Row"]=df["Bin"].str[0]
    df["Num"]=df["Bin"].str[1:].astype(int)
    moves=[]
    for material, group in df.groupby("Material"):
        if len(group)<2:
            continue
        sources=group[group["TotalStock"]>0].sort_values(by="Num", ascending=False).copy()
        targets=group.sort_values(by="Num", ascending=True).copy()
        for _, s in sources.iterrows():
            source_stock=float(s["TotalStock"])
            for t_idx, t in targets.iterrows():
                if int(t["Num"]) >= int(s["Num"]):
                    continue
                if same_row and t["Row"] != s["Row"]:
                    continue
                target_stock=float(targets.at[t_idx,"TotalStock"])
                target_cap=float(t["Capacity"])
                if target_stock >= target_cap:
                    continue
                space=target_cap-target_stock
                qty=min(source_stock, space)
                if qty>0:
                    moves.append({
                        "Material": material,
                        "Description": s["Description"],
                        "From": s["Bin"],
                        "To": t["Bin"],
                        "Qty": qty
                    })
                    source_stock -= qty
                    targets.at[t_idx,"TotalStock"]=target_stock+qty
                if source_stock<=0:
                    break
    return pd.DataFrame(moves)

Your `trual.txt` is already a valid “move list” output (material | from bin -> to bin | qty | description). Example lines like `285936 | D38 -> E04 | 5.00 | …` match the format your app prints. fileciteturn1file3L1-L7

Two important problems to fix before you trust it in the real world:

1) **Your SAP export bins look like `2A33`, `2A34`, …** in the XML you uploaded. fileciteturn1file0L38-L46  
   Your current regex expects `A33` style bins, so the app will miss bins unless you strip the leading digit(s). That’s why your workflow “Excel → trial” happened: Excel likely normalized the bin labels.

2) **Your Windows/Linux execution issues were tooling, but the logic issue is in the code**: you should normalize bin names in `parse_sap_xml()` (strip any leading digits) so you can feed the raw SAP XML directly.

### What I generated for you (from your uploaded `bins.xml`)
I parsed your `bins.xml` and generated clean move-lists:

- **Any-row moves** (can move between letters): **462 moves**
- **Same-row-only moves** (A→A, B→B, etc.): **233 moves**

### The code fix you need (bin normalization)
In both `app.py` and `parser.py`, right after you read `bin_name = parts[6]`, normalize it:

```python
import re

bin_name = parts[6].strip()
m = re.match(r'^\d+([A-Z]\d+)$', bin_name)
if m:
    bin_name = m.group(1)
```

That makes the app handle `2A33` → `A33` automatically, so you don’t need Excel as a middleman.

import sys
import os
import re
import pandas as pd
import xml.etree.ElementTree as ET
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import filedialog, messagebox, ttk

class BinConsolidatorApp:
    def __init__(self, root):
        self.root = root
        self.root.title("Plasti-Pak Line Clearance Optimizer")
        self.root.geometry("800x600")
        
        self.file_path = tk.StringVar()
        self.results_text = None
        
        self.setup_ui()
        
    def setup_ui(self):
        main_frame = ttk.Frame(self.root, padding="10")
        main_frame.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True)
        
        file_frame = ttk.LabelFrame(main_frame, text="Input SAP Snapshot", padding="10")
        file_frame.pack(fill=tk.X, pady=5)
        
        ttk.Entry(file_frame, textvariable=self.file_path, width=70).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)
        ttk.Button(file_frame, text="Browse", command=self.browse_file).pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        
        btn_frame = ttk.Frame(main_frame, padding="10")
        btn_frame.pack(fill=tk.X)
        
        ttk.Button(btn_frame, text="Generate Extraction List", command=self.process_data).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)
        ttk.Button(btn_frame, text="Save Move List", command=self.save_results).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)
        
        results_frame = ttk.LabelFrame(main_frame, text="Extraction List (Goal: Clear Bins 47 -> 02)", padding="10")
        results_frame.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True, pady=5)
        
        self.results_text = tk.Text(results_frame, wrap=tk.WORD)
        self.results_text.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True)
        
        scrollbar = ttk.Scrollbar(self.results_text, orient=tk.VERTICAL, command=self.results_text.yview)
        scrollbar.pack(side=tk.RIGHT, fill=tk.Y)
        self.results_text.configure(yscrollcommand=scrollbar.set)

    def browse_file(self):
        filename = filedialog.askopenfilename(filetypes=[("XML files", "*.xml"), ("All files", "*.*")])
        if filename:
            self.file_path.set(filename)

    def parse_sap_xml(self, file_path):
        try:
            tree = ET.parse(file_path)
            root = tree.getroot()
            ns = {'ss': 'urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet'}
            data_rows = []
            for row in root.findall('.//ss:Row', ns):
                for cell in row.findall('ss:Cell', ns):
                    data_node = cell.find('ss:Data', ns)
                    if data_node is not None and data_node.text:
                        lines = data_node.text.split('\n')
                        for line in lines:
                            if line.startswith('|') and 'StorageBin' not in line and '---' not in line:
                                parts = [p.strip() for p in line.split('|')]
                                if len(parts) > 11:
                                    try:
                                        bin_name = parts[6]
                                        material = parts[7]
                                        description = parts[8]
                                        total_stock = float(parts[11].replace(',', '')) if parts[11] else 0.0
                                        capacity = float(parts[17].replace(',', '')) if len(parts) > 17 and parts[17] else 0.0
                                        data_rows.append({
                                            'Bin': bin_name,
                                            'Material': material,
                                            'Description': description,
                                            'TotalStock': total_stock,
                                            'Capacity': capacity
                                        })
                                    except (ValueError, IndexError):
                                        continue
            return pd.DataFrame(data_rows)
        except Exception as e:
            messagebox.showerror("Error", f"Failed to parse XML: {e}")
            return None

    def process_data(self):
        path = self.file_path.get()
        if not path:
            messagebox.showwarning("Warning", "Please select a file first.")
            return
        df = self.parse_sap_xml(path)
        if df is None or df.empty: return
        
        pattern = re.compile(r'^([A-G])(0[2-9]|[1-3][0-9]|4[0-7])$')
        df['Match'] = df['Bin'].apply(lambda x: pattern.match(x))
        df_filtered = df[df['Match'].notnull()].copy()
        if df_filtered.empty:
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "No bins found in the A02-G47 range.")
            return

        df_filtered['Row'] = df_filtered['Bin'].str[0]
        df_filtered['Num'] = df_filtered['Bin'].str[1:].astype(int)
        
        moves = []
        for material, group in df_filtered.groupby('Material'):
            if len(group) < 2: continue
            
            # EXTRACTION LOGIC:
            # Source: Bins with HIGHEST Num (closest to line)
            # Target: Bins with LOWEST Num (further from line)
            
            # Sort group to find sources (highest Num first)
            sources = group[group['TotalStock'] > 0].sort_values(by='Num', ascending=False)
            # Sort group to find targets (lowest Num first)
            targets = group.sort_values(by='Num', ascending=True)
            
            for s_idx, s_row in sources.iterrows():
                source_bin = s_row['Bin']
                source_num = s_row['Num']
                source_stock = s_row['TotalStock']
                
                for t_idx, t_row in targets.iterrows():
                    target_bin = t_row['Bin']
                    target_num = t_row['Num']
                    
                    # Only move from high number to lower number
                    if target_num >= source_num: continue
                    
                    target_cap = t_row['Capacity']
                    target_stock = t_row['TotalStock']
                    
                    if target_stock >= target_cap: continue
                    
                    space = target_cap - target_stock
                    move_qty = min(source_stock, space)
                    
                    if move_qty > 0:
                        moves.append({
                            'Material': material,
                            'Desc': s_row['Description'],
                            'From': source_bin,
                            'To': target_bin,
                            'Qty': move_qty
                        })
                        source_stock -= move_qty
                        targets.at[t_idx, 'TotalStock'] += move_qty
                        
                    if source_stock <= 0: break
        
        self.display_results(moves)

    def display_results(self, moves):
        self.results_text.delete(1.0, tk.END)
        if not moves:
            self.results_text.insert(tk.END, "No extraction moves found. Bins near the line are already clear or no space further back.")
            return
        self.results_text.insert(tk.END, f"Found {len(moves)} extraction moves to clear the line:\n\n")
        self.results_text.insert(tk.END, f"{'MATERIAL':<12} | {'FROM (LINE)':<11} -> {'TO (BACK)':<10} | {'QTY':<6} | {'DESCRIPTION'}\n")
        self.results_text.insert(tk.END, "-" * 90 + "\n")
        for m in moves:
            line = f"{m['Material']:<12} | {m['From']:<11} -> {m['To']:<10} | {m['Qty']:<6.2f} | {m['Desc']}\n"
            self.results_text.insert(tk.END, line)

    def save_results(self):
        content = self.results_text.get(1.0, tk.END)
        if not content.strip(): return
        filename = filedialog.asksaveasfilename(defaultextension=".txt", filetypes=[("Text files", "*.txt")])
        if filename:
            with open(filename, 'w') as f: f.write(content)
            messagebox.showinfo("Success", "Extraction list saved.")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    root = tk.Tk()
    app = BinConsolidatorApp(root)
    root.mainloop()

import xml.etree.ElementTree as ET
import re
import pandas as pd

def parse_sap_xml(file_path):
    try:
        tree = ET.parse(file_path)
        root = tree.getroot()
        ns = {'ss': 'urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet'}
        
        data_rows = []
        for row in root.findall('.//ss:Row', ns):
            for cell in row.findall('ss:Cell', ns):
                data_node = cell.find('ss:Data', ns)
                if data_node is not None and data_node.text:
                    lines = data_node.text.split('\n')
                    for line in lines:
                        if line.startswith('|') and 'StorageBin' not in line and '---' not in line:
                            parts = [p.strip() for p in line.split('|')]
                            # The header suggests:
                            # 0: empty (before first |)
                            # 1: Typ
                            # 2: Sec
                            # 3: P
                            # 4: R
                            # 5: E
                            # 6: StorageBin
                            # 7: Materia
                            # 8: Material Description
                            # 9: Avail.stock
                            # 10: BUn
                            # 11: Total Stock
                            # ...
                            # 17: Total capacity
                            # 18: Remain.capacity
                            if len(parts) > 11:
                                try:
                                    bin_name = parts[6]
                                    material = parts[7]
                                    description = parts[8]
                                    total_stock = float(parts[11].replace(',', '')) if parts[11] else 0.0
                                    capacity = float(parts[17].replace(',', '')) if len(parts) > 17 and parts[17] else 0.0
                                    
                                    data_rows.append({
                                        'Bin': bin_name,
                                        'Material': material,
                                        'Description': description,
                                        'TotalStock': total_stock,
                                        'Capacity': capacity
                                    })
                                except (ValueError, IndexError):
                                    continue
        
        return pd.DataFrame(data_rows)
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"Error parsing XML: {e}")
        return None

if __name__ == "__main__":
    df = parse_sap_xml('/home/ubuntu/upload/bins.xml')
    if df is not None:
        # Filter for A02-G47
        # Pattern: [A-G](0[2-9]|[1-3][0-9]|4[0-7])
        pattern = re.compile(r'^[A-G](0[2-9]|[1-4][0-9])$') # Broadened slightly to check
        df_filtered = df[df['Bin'].apply(lambda x: bool(pattern.match(x)))]
        print(f"Total rows found: {len(df)}")
        print(f"Rows in A-G range: {len(df_filtered)}")
        if not df_filtered.empty:
            print(df_filtered.head(20))
        else:
            print("No bins matching A-G range found. Sample bins:")
            print(df['Bin'].head(20))
    else:
        print("Failed to parse data.")

sort targets ascending by Num, with stock < capacity and number below threshold\n    targets = group[(group['TotalStock'] < group['Capacity']) & (group['Num'] < threshold)].sort_values(by='Num', ascending=True)\n    # convert DataFrame to dictionaries to update\n    targets_stock = targets['TotalStock'].to_dict()\n\n    # We'll keep track of modifications in group for next sources\n    for s_idx, s_row in sources.iterrows():\n        source_bin = s_row['Bin']\n        source_desc = s_row['Description']\n        source_stock = s_row['TotalStock']\n        source_num = s_row['Num']\n        # skip if target is not further back than source (can't move to equal or larger num)\n            if target_num >= source_num:\n                continue\n            # ensure not near-line (already filtered by threshold)\n            # compute capacity left\n            target_cap = target_row['Capacity']\n            target_current_stock = targets_stock[t_idx]\n            space = target_cap - target_current_stock\n            if space <= 0:\n                continue\n            move_qty = min(source_stock, space)\n            if move_qty > 0:\n                moves.append({\n                    'Material': material,\n                    'Desc': source_desc,\n                    'From': source_bin,\n                    'To': target_bin,\n                    'Qty': move_qty\n                })\n                source_stock -= move_qty\n                # update target stock\n                targets_stock[t_idx] += move_qty\n            if source_stock <= 0:\n                break\n\n# sort moves by material maybe\nprint('Total moves:', len(moves))\nprint(moves[:10])\nPY"], "timeout": 100000}

{"cmd":["bash","-lc","apply_patch <<'EOF'\n*** Begin Patch\n*** Add File: consolidate_bins.py\n+\"\"\"\n+consolidate_bins.py\n+====================\n+\n+Command‑line utility to generate a line‑clearance consolidation plan from a\n+SAP snapshot export.  The export should be an XML spreadsheet formatted like\n+the one used in the Plasti‑Pak line‑clearance workflow: each row begins with\n+a `|` character and contains storage bin, material, description, stock and\n+capacity values separated by pipes.  Bins are named with a letter (A‑G) and\n+two digits, optionally prefixed with digits (e.g., `2A33` or `A33`).\n+\n+The utility reads the snapshot, normalizes the bin names, filters for bins\n+between A02 and G47 inclusive, and then generates a list of moves to clear\n+the bins nearest the line.  Material from bins with higher numeric values\n+(closer to the line) is moved into bins with lower numeric values (farther\n+from the line) until the high‑numbered bins are emptied or the low‑numbered\n+bins are full.  Bins with numbers greater than or equal to the specified\n+`threshold` are never used as targets, so they remain available near the\n+line.  The default threshold is 40, meaning bins 40‑47 will only act as\n+sources.\n+\n+Usage:\n+    python consolidate_bins.py input.xml output.csv [threshold]\n+\n+Examples:\n+    python consolidate_bins.py bins.xml moves.csv\n+    python consolidate_bins.py snapshot_20260101.xml plan.csv 38\n+\n+Outputs a CSV file with columns: Material,Description,FromBin,ToBin,Quantity.\n+\"\"\"\n+\n+import sys\n+import re\n+import xml.etree.ElementTree as ET\n+import pandas as pd\n+from typing import List\n+\n+\n+def normalize_bin(bin_name: str) -> str:\n+    \"\"\"Normalize bin names by stripping leading digits and zero‑padding.\n+\n+    Examples:\n+        '2A3'  -> 'A03'\n+        'A3'   -> 'A03'\n+        'A12'  -> 'A12'\n+\n+    If the bin name does not match the expected pattern, it is returned\n+    unchanged.\n+    \"\"\"\n+    m = re.match(r'^(\\d+)?([A-G])(\\d+)$', bin_name)\n+    if m:\n+        row_letter = m.group(2)\n+        num = int(m.group(3))\n+        return f\"{row_letter}{num:02d}\"\n+    return bin_name\n+\n+\n+def parse_snapshot(xml_path: str) -> pd.DataFrame:\n+    \"\"\"Parse the SAP XML snapshot and return a DataFrame of relevant fields.\n+\n+    The DataFrame has columns:\n+        BinRaw, Material, Description, TotalStock, Capacity, Bin\n+\n+    Rows with missing or malformed numeric data are skipped.\n+    \"\"\"\n+    tree = ET.parse(xml_path)\n+    root = tree.getroot()\n+    ns = {'ss': 'urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet'}\n+    rows: List[dict] = []\n+    # Iterate over all text cells.  Each line within a cell is separated\n+    # by newline characters.  Only lines starting with '|' contain the\n+    # snapshot data; header lines and dashes are ignored.\n+    for cell in root.findall('.//ss:Data', ns):\n+        text = cell.text or ''\n+        for line in text.split('\\n'):\n+            if not line.startswith('|'):\n+                continue\n+            if 'StorageBin' in line or '---' in line:\n+                continue\n+            parts = [p.strip() for p in line.split('|')]\n+            # The expected fields are at fixed positions:\n+            # 6: StorageBin, 7: Material, 8: Description,\n+            # 11: TotalStock, 17: Capacity\n+            try:\n+                bin_raw = parts[6]\n+                material = parts[7]\n+                desc = parts[8]\n+                total_stock = float(parts[11].replace(',', '')) if parts[11] else 0.0\n+                capacity = float(parts[17].replace(',', '')) if len(parts) > 17 and parts[17] else 0.0\n+            except (IndexError, ValueError):\n+                continue\n+            norm_bin = normalize_bin(bin_raw)\n+            rows.append({\n+                'BinRaw': bin_raw,\n+                'Material': material,\n+                'Description': desc,\n+                'TotalStock': total_stock,\n+                'Capacity': capacity,\n+                'Bin': norm_bin,\n+            })\n+    return pd.DataFrame(rows)\n+\n+\n+def generate_moves(df: pd.DataFrame, threshold: int = 40) -> List[dict]:\n+    \"\"\"Generate consolidation moves from a DataFrame of snapshot data.\n+\n+    Parameters\n+    ----------\n+    df : pandas.DataFrame\n+        DataFrame with columns Bin, Material, Description, TotalStock, Capacity,\n+        Row, Num.  Only rows matching pattern A02–G47 should be included.\n+    threshold : int\n+        Bins with numeric part >= threshold are considered near the line and\n+        will never be used as targets.  Default is 40.\n+\n+    Returns\n+    -------\n+    List[dict]\n+        Each dict has keys: Material, Description, FromBin, ToBin, Quantity.\n+    \"\"\"\n+    moves: List[dict] = []\n+    # Group by material to avoid mixing different materials in the same bin.\n+    for material, group in df.groupby('Material'):\n+        if len(group) < 2:\n+            # A single bin cannot be consolidated.\n+            continue\n+        group = group.copy()\n+        # Sort source bins (those with stock) by descending numeric value (closer to line).\n+        sources = group[group['TotalStock'] > 0].sort_values(by='Num', ascending=False)\n+        # Sort target bins by ascending numeric value (further from line),\n+        # but only bins with space and number below threshold are candidates.\n+        targets = group[(group['TotalStock'] < group['Capacity']) & (group['Num'] < threshold)].sort_values(by='Num')\n+        # Keep track of updated stock in targets\n+        target_stock = targets['TotalStock'].to_dict()\n+        for _, src in sources.iterrows():\n+            from_bin = src['Bin']\n+            desc = src['Description']\n+            available = src['TotalStock']\n+            src_num = src['Num']\n+            if available <= 0:\n+                continue\n+            for t_idx in targets.index:\n+                tgt = targets.loc[t_idx]\n+                to_bin = tgt['Bin']\n+                tgt_num = tgt['Num']\n+                if tgt_num >= src_num:\n+                    # Only move to bins further back (lower number)\n+                    continue\n+                cap = tgt['Capacity']\n+                curr = target_stock[t_idx]\n+                space = cap - curr\n+                if space <= 0:\n+                    continue\n+                qty = min(available, space)\n+                if qty > 0:\n+                    moves.append({\n+                        'Material': material,\n+                        'Description': desc,\n+                        'FromBin': from_bin,\n+                        'ToBin': to_bin,\n+                        'Quantity': qty,\n+                    })\n+                    available -= qty\n+                    target_stock[t_idx] += qty\n+                if available <= 0:\n+                    break\n+    return moves\n+\n+\n+def main(args: List[str]) -> None:\n+    if len(args) < 2 or len(args) > 3:\n+        print(\"Usage: python consolidate_bins.py <input.xml> <output.csv> [threshold]\", file=sys.stderr)\n+        sys.exit(1)\n+    input_path = args[0]\n+    output_path = args[1]\n+    threshold = int(args[2]) if len(args) == 3 else 40\n+    # Parse snapshot and normalize bins\n+    df = parse_snapshot(input_path)\n+    # Filter for bins A02–G47\n+    pattern = re.compile(r'^[A-G](0[2-9]|[1-3][0-9]|4[0-7])$')\n+    df = df[df['Bin'].apply(lambda x: bool(pattern.match(x)))].copy()\n+    if df.empty:\n+        print(\"No bins in range A02–G47 found in the snapshot.\")\n+        return\n+    # Add row and numeric part for sorting\n+    df['Row'] = df['Bin'].str[0]\n+    df['Num'] = df['Bin'].str[1:].astype(int)\n+    moves = generate_moves(df, threshold=threshold)\n+    # Convert to DataFrame and write CSV\n+    moves_df = pd.DataFrame(moves)\n+    moves_df.to_csv(output_path, index=False)\n+    print(f\"Generated {len(moves_df)} move(s) to {output_path}.\")\n+\n+\n+if __name__ == '__main__':\n+    main(sys.argv[1:])\n*** End Patch\nEOF"]}

[ASSISTANT]
Here’s a standalone utility you can use repeatedly with any SAP snapshot that follows the same XML format.  It reads the snapshot, normalizes bin names (e.g. `2A33` → `A33`), and generates a move list that empties bins nearest the lines by moving their contents into bins farther back.  By default it never fills bins numbered 40–47, so those stay open for new stock; you can change that by supplying a different threshold.

- **Script:** `consolidate_bins.py` – run it with `python consolidate_bins.py <snapshot.xml> <output.csv> [threshold]` and it writes a CSV move list.  For example, to generate a plan from `bins.xml` and leave bins 40–47 empty:  
  ```bash
  python consolidate_bins.py bins.xml my_moves.csv 40
  ```
  The optional third argument lets you choose how far back to keep bins open.

- **Move list for the uploaded snapshot:** I generated a move list using the default threshold of 40.  It contains 461 moves and shows which bin each pallet should come from and where it should go.

You can download both the script and the example output here:

* [consolidate_bins.py]({{file:file-AJKBL1a23xVjuw2mxG92UU}})
* [line_clearance_moves_general.csv]({{file:file-S78DhLbmbPF8X7Hs7yA7i6}})

This approach keeps the high‑numbered bins empty, consolidates identical materials across rows, and ensures that partially filled bins are topped up before opening new ones, so operators don’t have to move pallets far when restocking. Let me know if you need help running it on your own snapshots or adjusting the threshold.

You can’t magically conjure a Windows binary on a Linux host; PyInstaller isn’t a cross‑compiler. The only reliable way to get `Consolidator.exe` is to run PyInstaller **on a Windows machine** where Python is installed. PyInstaller’s own docs make it clear that you run it from the directory containing your script and it writes the `.spec`, `build`, and `dist` folders, with the bundled executable in `dist`【331818895627038†L66-L91】.

Here’s what you should do on your Windows PC:

1. **Download the script** (`consolidate_bins.py`) from our previous exchange. Save it somewhere, e.g., `C:\Scripts\consolidate_bins.py`.  
2. **Install Python and dependencies:** get a proper Python from python.org (tick “Add Python to PATH”), then open PowerShell and run:  
   ```powershell
   python -m pip install --upgrade pip pandas pyinstaller
   ```
3. **Build the executable:** move to the folder where you saved the script and run:  
   ```powershell
   cd C:\Scripts
   pyinstaller --onefile --name Consolidator consolidate_bins.py
   ```  
   PyInstaller will analyze `consolidate_bins.py`, write a `Consolidator.spec`, create `build` and `dist` folders, and drop `Consolidator.exe` into the `dist` directory【331818895627038†L66-L91】. Use `--onefile` for a single‑file exe and `--name` to set the filename.
4. **Run it:** copy `Consolidator.exe` wherever you want, and execute it from the command prompt. Use it exactly like the Python script:  
   ```cmd
   Consolidator.exe snapshot.xml output.csv 40
   ```

If you need to brand it further (icon, splash), PyInstaller offers options like `--icon` and `--windowed`【331818895627038†L180-L183】, but the above is the bare minimum. And remember: building on Windows is mandatory—PyInstaller explicitly states it creates the platform‑specific binary on the host you run it on【331818895627038†L66-L91】, so no amount of Linux tinkering will spit out a real `.exe`.

Without more detail it’s hard to diagnose, but there are two common issues that cause a freshly built .exe to appear to “not work”:

1. **Missing modules during build.**  When bundling with PyInstaller, you need to tell it to collect all of pandas’ dependencies.  Add the `--collect-all pandas` option so PyInstaller doesn’t miss any of pandas’ internal modules【331818895627038†L66-L91】.  For example:
   ```powershell
   cd C:\Scripts
   pyinstaller --onefile --name Consolidator --collect-all pandas consolidate_bins.py
   ```
   This creates a single‑file `Consolidator.exe` in the `dist` folder【331818895627038†L66-L91】.

2. **Running it incorrectly.**  The resulting program is a command‑line tool, so if you just double‑click it, it will flash open and exit immediately.  You need to run it from a Command Prompt and pass the snapshot and output filenames, for example:
   ```cmd
   Consolidator.exe snapshot.xml output.csv 40
   ```
   Replace `snapshot.xml` with your SAP snapshot and `output.csv` with the filename you want for the move list.  The optional `40` controls how far back to leave bins empty (bins numbered 40–47 stay empty by default).

If you still see an error, please copy and paste the error message so I can help troubleshoot further.

Only bins matching the A02–G47 pattern are\n+        included.  Bins with Num >= threshold are not used as targets.\n+        \"\"\"\n+        moves: list[dict] = []\n+        # Group by material\n+        for material, group in df.groupby('Material'):\n+            if len(group) < 2:\n+                continue\n+            group = group.copy()\n+            # Bins near the line are already clear or no space further back.\")\n+            return\n+        self.results_text.insert(tk.END, f\"Found {len(moves)} moves:\\n\\n\")\n+        header = f\"{'MATERIAL':<12} | {'FROM':<9} -> {'TO':<5} | {'QTY':<7} | DESCRIPTION\\n\"\n+        self.results_text.insert(tk.END, header)\n+        self.results_text.insert(tk.END, \"-\" * (len(header) + 20) + \"\\n\")\n+        for m in moves:\n+            line = f\"{m['Material']:<12} | {m['FromBin']:<9} -> {m['ToBin']:<5} | {m['Quantity']:<7.2f} | {m['Description']}\\n\"\n+            self.results_text.insert(tk.END, line)\n+\n+    def save_results(self) -> None:\n+        \"\"\"Save the displayed results to a text file.\"\"\"\n+        if self.results_text is None:\n+            return\n+        content = self.results_text.get(1.0, tk.END)\n+        if not content.strip():\n+            return\n+        filename = filedialog.asksaveasfilename(defaultextension=\".txt\", filetypes=[(\"Text files\", \"*.txt\"), (\"All files\", \"*.*\")])\n+        if filename:\n+            try:\n+                with open(filename, 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:\n+                    f.write(content)\n+                messagebox.showinfo(\"Success\", \"Results saved successfully.\")\n+            except Exception as e:\n+                messagebox.showerror(\"Error\", f\"Failed to save file: {e}\")\n+\n+\n+if __name__ == '__main__':\n+    root = tk.Tk()\n+    app = ConsolidatorApp(root)\n+    root.mainloop()\n*** End Patch\nEOF"]}

[ASSISTANT]
Here’s a proper **interactive** version of the program. It uses a Tkinter GUI: you pick the XML snapshot, set the “target threshold” (which bins to leave open), click a button, and it spits out the consolidation moves in a scrollable window. There’s also a “Save Results” button to dump the list to a text file. The threshold defaults to 40 (so bins 40–47 stay empty) but you can change it via a spinbox.

- **Download the Python GUI script**: {{file:file-8gz1goQD7jUqYCcBhNMKYY}}

If you run it directly with Python on Windows, it’ll pop up the window automatically (provided you installed Python with Tcl/Tk). To make it a standalone Windows app named `Consolidator.exe`, you’ll need to build it with PyInstaller on a Windows machine. The docs explain that you run PyInstaller from the folder containing your script; it writes a `.spec`, a `build` directory, and a `dist` directory with the executable inside【331818895627038†L66-L91】. Use this command so pandas and the GUI get bundled correctly:

```powershell
cd C:\wherever\you\put\the\script
python -m pip install pyinstaller pandas
pyinstaller --onefile --windowed --name Consolidator --collect-all pandas consolidator_gui.py
```

That creates `Consolidator.exe` inside `dist\`. Double‑clicking it launches the GUI. You don’t need the console anymore because `--windowed` hides it.

Let me know if you run into trouble packaging it or need tweaks to the interface.

"""
Interactive GUI application for line-clearance consolidation.

This Tkinter application allows the user to load a SAP snapshot XML file,
choose a threshold for how far back to consolidate bins (default 40), and
generate a list of moves that empty bins near the line.  Material from bins
with higher numeric values (closer to the line) is moved into bins with
lower numeric values (farther from the line) until the high-numbered bins
are emptied or the low-numbered bins are full.  Bins with numbers greater
than or equal to the selected threshold are never used as targets, so they
remain open near the line.

The results are displayed in a scrollable text widget and can be saved to a
text file.  The program relies only on the pandas and tkinter libraries.

Usage:
    python consolidator_gui.py

On Windows, you can package this script into a standalone executable using
PyInstaller.  For example:

    pyinstaller --onefile --windowed --name Consolidator --collect-all pandas consolidator_gui.py

This will generate `Consolidator.exe` in the `dist` folder.  When run, it
opens a window where you can browse for the XML snapshot and generate a
consolidation plan.
"""

import re
import pandas as pd
import xml.etree.ElementTree as ET
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import filedialog, messagebox, ttk


def normalize_bin(bin_name: str) -> str:
    """Normalize bin names by stripping leading digits and zero-padding.

    Examples:
        '2A3'  -> 'A03'
        'A3'   -> 'A03'
        'A12'  -> 'A12'

    If the bin name does not match the expected pattern, it is returned
    unchanged.
    """
    m = re.match(r'^(\d+)?([A-G])(\d+)$', bin_name)
    if m:
        row_letter = m.group(2)
        num = int(m.group(3))
        return f"{row_letter}{num:02d}"
    return bin_name


class ConsolidatorApp:
    def __init__(self, root: tk.Tk) -> None:
        self.root = root
        self.root.title("Consolidator – Line Clearance Optimizer")
        self.root.geometry("900x650")
        # Variables to hold file path and threshold
        self.file_path = tk.StringVar()
        self.threshold_var = tk.IntVar(value=40)
        self.results_text: tk.Text | None = None
        # Build the UI
        self.setup_ui()

    def setup_ui(self) -> None:
        """Construct the user interface."""
        main_frame = ttk.Frame(self.root, padding="10")
        main_frame.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True)

        # File selection frame
        file_frame = ttk.LabelFrame(main_frame, text="Input SAP Snapshot", padding="10")
        file_frame.pack(fill=tk.X, pady=5)
        ttk.Entry(file_frame, textvariable=self.file_path, width=70).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)
        ttk.Button(file_frame, text="Browse", command=self.browse_file).pack(side=tk.LEFT)

        # Threshold frame
        thresh_frame = ttk.Frame(main_frame, padding="5")
        thresh_frame.pack(fill=tk.X)
        ttk.Label(thresh_frame, text="Target threshold (bin numbers < this value)", padding="5").pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        threshold_spin = ttk.Spinbox(
            thresh_frame,
            from_=2,
            to=47,
            increment=1,
            textvariable=self.threshold_var,
            width=5,
        )
        threshold_spin.pack(side=tk.LEFT)

        # Buttons for processing and saving
        btn_frame = ttk.Frame(main_frame, padding="10")
        btn_frame.pack(fill=tk.X)
        ttk.Button(btn_frame, text="Generate Consolidation Plan", command=self.process_data).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)
        ttk.Button(btn_frame, text="Save Results", command=self.save_results).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)

        # Results display frame
        results_frame = ttk.LabelFrame(main_frame, text="Consolidation Moves", padding="10")
        results_frame.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True, pady=5)
        self.results_text = tk.Text(results_frame, wrap=tk.WORD)
        self.results_text.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True)
        scrollbar = ttk.Scrollbar(results_frame, orient=tk.VERTICAL, command=self.results_text.yview)
        scrollbar.pack(side=tk.RIGHT, fill=tk.Y)
        self.results_text.configure(yscrollcommand=scrollbar.set)

    def browse_file(self) -> None:
        """Open a file dialog to choose the XML snapshot."""
        filename = filedialog.askopenfilename(filetypes=[("XML files", "*.xml"), ("All files", "*.*")])
        if filename:
            self.file_path.set(filename)

    def parse_sap_xml(self, file_path: str) -> pd.DataFrame | None:
        """Parse the SAP snapshot XML into a DataFrame of bins.

        Returns None on failure.
        """
        try:
            tree = ET.parse(file_path)
            root = tree.getroot()
            ns = {'ss': 'urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet'}
            rows = []
            # iterate over all data cells
            for cell in root.findall('.//ss:Data', ns):
                text = cell.text or ''
                for line in text.split('\n'):
                    if not line.startswith('|'):
                        continue
                    if 'StorageBin' in line or '---' in line:
                        continue
                    parts = [p.strip() for p in line.split('|')]
                    if len(parts) > 11:
                        try:
                            raw_bin = parts[6]
                            material = parts[7]
                            desc = parts[8]
                            total_stock = float(parts[11].replace(',', '')) if parts[11] else 0.0
                            capacity = float(parts[17].replace(',', '')) if len(parts) > 17 and parts[17] else 0.0
                        except (IndexError, ValueError):
                            continue
                        norm_bin = normalize_bin(raw_bin)
                        rows.append({
                            'Bin': norm_bin,
                            'Material': material,
                            'Description': desc,
                            'TotalStock': total_stock,
                            'Capacity': capacity,
                        })
            df = pd.DataFrame(rows)
            return df
        except Exception as e:
            messagebox.showerror("Error", f"Failed to parse XML: {e}")
            return None

    def generate_moves(self, df: pd.DataFrame, threshold: int) -> list[dict]:
        """Generate consolidation moves from the given DataFrame.

        The DataFrame should have columns Bin, Material, Description, TotalStock,
        Capacity, Row, and Num.  Only bins matching the A02–G47 pattern are
        included.  Bins with Num >= threshold are not used as targets.
        """
        moves: list[dict] = []
        # Group by material
        for material, group in df.groupby('Material'):
            if len(group) < 2:
                continue
            group = group.copy()
            # Sort sources descending by Num (closer to line) and only those with stock
            sources = group[group['TotalStock'] > 0].sort_values(by='Num', ascending=False)
            # Sort targets ascending by Num (farther from line), only with space and below threshold
            targets = group[(group['TotalStock'] < group['Capacity']) & (group['Num'] < threshold)].sort_values(by='Num', ascending=True)
            target_stock = targets['TotalStock'].to_dict()
            for _, src in sources.iterrows():
                src_bin = src['Bin']
                desc = src['Description']
                available = src['TotalStock']
                src_num = src['Num']
                if available <= 0:
                    continue
                for t_idx in targets.index:
                    tgt = targets.loc[t_idx]
                    tgt_bin = tgt['Bin']
                    tgt_num = tgt['Num']
                    # Only move to bins further back
                    if tgt_num >= src_num:
                        continue
                    cap = tgt['Capacity']
                    curr = target_stock[t_idx]
                    space = cap - curr
                    if space <= 0:
                        continue
                    qty = min(available, space)
                    if qty > 0:
                        moves.append({
                            'Material': material,
                            'Description': desc,
                            'FromBin': src_bin,
                            'ToBin': tgt_bin,
                            'Quantity': qty,
                        })
                        available -= qty
                        target_stock[t_idx] += qty
                    if available <= 0:
                        break
        return moves

    def process_data(self) -> None:
        """Parse the selected file and generate the move list."""
        path = self.file_path.get().strip()
        if not path:
            messagebox.showwarning("Warning", "Please select a file first.")
            return
        df = self.parse_sap_xml(path)
        if df is None or df.empty:
            return
        # Filter for bins A02–G47
        pattern = re.compile(r'^[A-G](0[2-9]|[1-3][0-9]|4[0-7])$')
        df = df[df['Bin'].apply(lambda x: bool(pattern.match(x)))].copy()
        if df.empty:
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "No bins found in the A02–G47 range.")

```powershell
@'
"""
Interactive GUI application for line-clearance consolidation.

This Tkinter application allows the user to load a SAP snapshot XML file,
choose a threshold for how far back to consolidate bins (default 40), and
generate a list of moves that empty bins near the line.  Material from bins
with higher numeric values (closer to the line) is moved into bins with
lower numeric values (farther from the line) until the high-numbered bins
are emptied or the low-numbered bins are full.  Bins with numbers greater
than or equal to the selected threshold are never used as targets, so they
remain open near the line.

The results are displayed in a scrollable text widget and can be saved to a
text file.  The program relies only on the pandas and tkinter libraries.

Usage:
    python consolidator_gui.py

On Windows, you can package this script into a standalone executable using
PyInstaller.  For example:

    pyinstaller --onefile --windowed --name Consolidator --collect-all pandas consolidator_gui.py

This will generate `Consolidator.exe` in the `dist` folder.  When run, it
opens a window where you can browse for the XML snapshot and generate a
consolidation plan.
"""

import re
import pandas as pd
import xml.etree.ElementTree as ET
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import filedialog, messagebox, ttk


def normalize_bin(bin_name: str) -> str:
    """Normalize bin names by stripping leading digits and zero-padding.

    Examples:
        '2A3'  -> 'A03'
        'A3'   -> 'A03'
        'A12'  -> 'A12'

    If the bin name does not match the expected pattern, it is returned
    unchanged.
    """
    m = re.match(r'^(\d+)?([A-G])(\d+)$', bin_name)
    if m:
        row_letter = m.group(2)
        num = int(m.group(3))
        return f"{row_letter}{num:02d}"
    return bin_name


class ConsolidatorApp:
    def __init__(self, root: tk.Tk) -> None:
        self.root = root
        self.root.title("Consolidator – Line Clearance Optimizer")
        self.root.geometry("900x650")
        self.file_path = tk.StringVar()
        self.threshold_var = tk.IntVar(value=40)
        self.results_text: tk.Text | None = None
        self.setup_ui()

    def setup_ui(self) -> None:
        main_frame = ttk.Frame(self.root, padding="10")
        main_frame.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True)

        file_frame = ttk.LabelFrame(main_frame, text="Input SAP Snapshot", padding="10")
        file_frame.pack(fill=tk.X, pady=5)
        ttk.Entry(file_frame, textvariable=self.file_path, width=70).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)
        ttk.Button(file_frame, text="Browse", command=self.browse_file).pack(side=tk.LEFT)

        thresh_frame = ttk.Frame(main_frame, padding="5")
        thresh_frame.pack(fill=tk.X)
        ttk.Label(thresh_frame, text="Target threshold (bin numbers < this value)", padding="5").pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        threshold_spin = ttk.Spinbox(
            thresh_frame,
            from_=2,
            to=47,
            increment=1,
            textvariable=self.threshold_var,
            width=5,
        )
        threshold_spin.pack(side=tk.LEFT)

        btn_frame = ttk.Frame(main_frame, padding="10")
        btn_frame.pack(fill=tk.X)
        ttk.Button(btn_frame, text="Generate Consolidation Plan", command=self.process_data).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)
        ttk.Button(btn_frame, text="Save Results", command=self.save_results).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)

        results_frame = ttk.LabelFrame(main_frame, text="Consolidation Moves", padding="10")
        results_frame.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True, pady=5)
        self.results_text = tk.Text(results_frame, wrap=tk.WORD)
        self.results_text.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True)
        scrollbar = ttk.Scrollbar(results_frame, orient=tk.VERTICAL, command=self.results_text.yview)
        scrollbar.pack(side=tk.RIGHT, fill=tk.Y)
        self.results_text.configure(yscrollcommand=scrollbar.set)

    def browse_file(self) -> None:
        filename = filedialog.askopenfilename(filetypes=[("XML files", "*.xml"), ("All files", "*.*")])
        if filename:
            self.file_path.set(filename)

    def parse_sap_xml(self, file_path: str) -> pd.DataFrame | None:
        try:
            tree = ET.parse(file_path)
            root = tree.getroot()
            ns = {'ss': 'urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet'}
            rows = []
            for cell in root.findall('.//ss:Data', ns):
                text = cell.text or ''
                for line in text.split('\n'):
                    if not line.startswith('|'):
                        continue
                    if 'StorageBin' in line or '---' in line:
                        continue
                    parts = [p.strip() for p in line.split('|')]
                    if len(parts) > 11:
                        try:
                            raw_bin = parts[6]
                            material = parts[7]
                            desc = parts[8]
                            total_stock = float(parts[11].replace(',', '')) if parts[11] else 0.0
                            capacity = float(parts[17].replace(',', '')) if len(parts) > 17 and parts[17] else 0.0
                        except (IndexError, ValueError):
                            continue
                        norm_bin = normalize_bin(raw_bin)
                        rows.append({
                            'Bin': norm_bin,
                            'Material': material,
                            'Description': desc,
                            'TotalStock': total_stock,
                            'Capacity': capacity,
                        })
            df = pd.DataFrame(rows)
            return df
        except Exception as e:
            messagebox.showerror("Error", f"Failed to parse XML: {e}")
            return None

    def generate_moves(self, df: pd.DataFrame, threshold: int) -> list[dict]:
        moves: list[dict] = []
        for material, group in df.groupby('Material'):
            if len(group) < 2:
                continue
            group = group.copy()
            sources = group[group['TotalStock'] > 0].sort_values(by='Num', ascending=False)
            targets = group[(group['TotalStock'] < group['Capacity']) & (group['Num'] < threshold)].sort_values(by='Num', ascending=True)
            target_stock = targets['TotalStock'].to_dict()
            for _, src in sources.iterrows():
                src_bin = src['Bin']
                desc = src['Description']
                available = src['TotalStock']
                src_num = src['Num']
                if available <= 0:
                    continue
                for t_idx in targets.index:
                    tgt = targets.loc[t_idx]
                    tgt_bin = tgt['Bin']
                    tgt_num = tgt['Num']
                    if tgt_num >= src_num:
                        continue
                    cap = tgt['Capacity']
                    curr = target_stock[t_idx]
                    space = cap - curr
                    if space <= 0:
                        continue
                    qty = min(available, space)
                    if qty > 0:
                        moves.append({
                            'Material': material,
                            'Description': desc,
                            'FromBin': src_bin,
                            'ToBin': tgt_bin,
                            'Quantity': qty,
                        })
                        available -= qty
                        target_stock[t_idx] += qty
                    if available <= 0:
                        break
        return moves

    def process_data(self) -> None:
        path = self.file_path.get().strip()
        if not path:
            messagebox.showwarning("Warning", "Please select a file first.")
            return
        df = self.parse_sap_xml(path)
        if df is None or df.empty:
            return
        pattern = re.compile(r'^[A-G](0[2-9]|[1-3][0-9]|4[0-7])$')
        df = df[df['Bin'].apply(lambda x: bool(pattern.match(x)))].copy()
        if df.empty:
            messagebox.showinfo("Info", "No bins found in the A02–G47 range.")
            return
        df['Row'] = df['Bin'].str[0]
        df['Num'] = df['Bin'].str[1:].astype(int)
        threshold = self.threshold_var.get()
        moves = self.generate_moves(df, threshold)
        self.display_results(moves)

    def display_results(self, moves: list[dict]) -> None:
        if self.results_text is None:
            return
        self.results_text.delete(1.0, tk.END)
        if not moves:
            self.results_text.insert(tk.END, "No consolidation moves found. Bins near the line are already clear or no space further back.")
            return
        self.results_text.insert(tk.END, f"Found {len(moves)} moves:\n\n")
        header = f"{'MATERIAL':<12} | {'FROM':<9} -> {'TO':<5} | {'QTY':<7} | DESCRIPTION\n"
        self.results_text.insert(tk.END, header)
        self.results_text.insert(tk.END, "-" * (len(header) + 20) + "\n")
        for m in moves:
            line = f"{m['Material']:<12} | {m['FromBin']:<9} -> {m['ToBin']:<5} | {m['Quantity']:<7.2f} | {m['Description']}\n"
            self.results_text.insert(tk.END, line)

    def save_results(self) -> None:
        if self.results_text is None:
            return
        content = self.results_text.get(1.0, tk.END)
        if not content.strip():
            return
        filename = filedialog.asksaveasfilename(defaultextension=".txt", filetypes=[("Text files", "*.txt"), ("All files", "*.*")])
        if filename:
            try:
                with open(filename, 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                    f.write(content)
                messagebox.showinfo("Success", "Results saved successfully.")
            except Exception as e:
                messagebox.showerror("Error", f"Failed to save file: {e}")


if __name__ == '__main__':
    root = tk.Tk()
    app = ConsolidatorApp(root)
    root.mainloop()
```

    root.mainloop()

[ASSISTANT]
Yes — **dynamic rows can work** — but your current version will **break on real SAP XML exports** and it also **accidentally limits moves to same-row only** (because you `groupby(['Material','Row'])`). If your goal is “move material to *any* bin that already holds that material, across *any* row,” then you must group by **Material only**.

Also: your XML parsing (`root.findall(".//Row")` and `"Cell/Data"`) won’t work for the SpreadsheetML SAP export you’ve been using (it uses the `urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet` namespace and the table is embedded in `ss:Data` text lines that start with `|`).

Below is the fix: **keep your dynamic row parser**, but swap in a **working SAP XML parser** and change the consolidation loop to work across **all rows**.

---

## 1) Replace your `normalize_bin()` with this (dynamic letters, any row)
Keeps exactly what you’re aiming for, but returns a clean dict-ish shape:

```python
def normalize_bin(bin_name: str):
    """
    Accepts bin formats like:
      '2A33' -> row='A',    num=33, bin='A33'
      'AA07' -> row='AA',   num=7,  bin='AA07'
      'R1'   -> row='R',    num=1,  bin='R01'
    If it doesn't match letters+digits, returns (None, None, original).
    """
    s = str(bin_name).strip()
    m = re.match(r'^(\d+)?([A-Za-z]+)(\d+)$', s)
    if not m:
        return None, None, s
    row = m.group(2).upper()
    num = int(m.group(3))
    # zero-pad to 2 digits (change to 3 if you use 001–999 bins)
    return row, num, f"{row}{num:02d}"
```

---

## 2) Use a real SAP SpreadsheetML parser (this is the big fix)
This matches the format you’ve already been exporting (pipe-delimited lines inside `ss:Data`):

```python
def parse_sap_snapshot_xml(path: str) -> pd.DataFrame:
    tree = ET.parse(path)
    root = tree.getroot()
    ns = {"ss": "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet"}

    rows = []
    for data_node in root.findall(".//ss:Data", ns):
        text = data_node.text or ""
        for line in text.split("\n"):
            if not line.startswith("|"):
                continue
            if "StorageBin" in line or "---" in line:
                continue

            parts = [p.strip() for p in line.split("|")]

            # These indices match your earlier app.py/parser.py extraction
            # Bin = parts[6], Material = parts[7], Desc = parts[8], Stock = parts[11], Capacity = parts[17]
            if len(parts) <= 11:
                continue

            raw_bin = parts[6]
            material = parts[7]
            desc = parts[8]
            stock = float(parts[11].replace(",", "")) if parts[11] else 0.0
            cap = float(parts[17].replace(",", "")) if len(parts) > 17 and parts[17] else 0.0

            row_id, bin_num, norm_bin = normalize_bin(raw_bin)

            rows.append({
                "Material": material,
                "BinRaw": raw_bin,
                "Bin": norm_bin,
                "Row": row_id,
                "BinNum": bin_num,
                "Qty": stock,
                "Capacity": cap,
                "Description": desc,
            })

    df = pd.DataFrame(rows)

    # Keep only bins we can reason about (letters+digits). Others stay out of the optimizer.
    df = df[df["BinNum"].notna()].copy()
    df["BinNum"] = df["BinNum"].astype(int)
    return df
```

---

## 3) The consolidation loop: **group by Material only**
This is the part that makes it “any row in warehouse”:

```python
def build_moves(df: pd.DataFrame, threshold: int):
    moves = []

    for material, group in df.groupby("Material"):
        if len(group) < 2:
            continue

        # SOURCES: bins we want to EMPTY (near-line), i.e., >= threshold
        sources = group[(group["BinNum"] >= threshold) & (group["Qty"] > 0)].sort_values("BinNum", ascending=False)

        # TARGETS: bins we can FILL (farther back), i.e., < threshold and not full
        targets = group[(group["BinNum"] < threshold) & (group["Qty"] < group["Capacity"])].sort_values("BinNum", ascending=True)

        if sources.empty or targets.empty:
            continue

        # We’ll track target quantities as we fill them
        tgt_qty = targets["Qty"].to_dict()

        for _, src in sources.iterrows():
            remaining = float(src["Qty"])
            if remaining <= 0:
                continue

            for t_idx in targets.index:
                cap = float(targets.loc[t_idx, "Capacity"])
                curr = float(tgt_qty[t_idx])
                space = cap - curr
                if space <= 0:
                    continue

                qty = min(space, remaining)
                if qty <= 0:
                    continue

                moves.append({
                    "Material": material,
                    "From": src["Bin"],
                    "To": targets.loc[t_idx, "Bin"],
                    "Qty": qty,
                    "Description": src["Description"],
                })

                remaining -= qty
                tgt_qty[t_idx] = curr + qty

                if remaining <= 0:
                    break

    return moves
```

This will move stock from **any** near-line bin to **any** existing bin for that material, regardless of row letters.

---

## 4) Where your code was going wrong (no sugar-coating)
- Your XML parsing won’t match SAP SpreadsheetML exports → **dead on arrival**.
- `groupby(['Material','Row'])` forces moves **within the same row** → contradicts your goal.
- You’re mutating `src`/`tgt` dict copies, not the DataFrame → fine for generating moves, but don’t assume df updates.
- Your threshold Entry + `IntVar` is fragile → use a `Spinbox` or validate the input.

import re
import pandas as pd
import xml.etree.ElementTree as ET
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import filedialog, messagebox, ttk

def normalize_bin(bin_name: str) -> str:
    """Extracts row (letters) and bin number (digits) dynamically."""
    # Matches optional prefix digits, then any letters (Row), then digits (Bin Number)
    m = re.match(r"^(\d+)?([a-zA-Z]+)(\d+)$", bin_name)
    if m:
        row_id = m.group(2).upper()
        num = int(m.group(3))
        return row_id, num, f"{row_id}{num:02d}"
    return None, None, bin_name

class ConsolidatorApp:
    def __init__(self, root: tk.Tk) -> None:
        self.root = root
        self.root.title("Consolidator – Dynamic Warehouse Optimizer")
        self.root.geometry("900x650")
        self.file_path = tk.StringVar()
        self.threshold = tk.IntVar(value=40)
        self._setup_ui()

    def _setup_ui(self):
        main_frame = ttk.Frame(self.root, padding="10")
        main_frame.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True)

        # File Selection
        file_frame = ttk.LabelFrame(main_frame, text="SAP Snapshot Selection", padding="10")
        file_frame.pack(fill=tk.X, pady=5)
        ttk.Entry(file_frame, textvariable=self.file_path, width=70).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)
        ttk.Button(file_frame, text="Browse", command=self.browse_file).pack(side=tk.LEFT)

        # Settings
        settings_frame = ttk.Frame(main_frame, padding="5")
        settings_frame.pack(fill=tk.X)
        ttk.Label(settings_frame, text="Empty Bins >= Threshold:").pack(side=tk.LEFT)
        ttk.Entry(settings_frame, textvariable=self.threshold, width=10).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)
        ttk.Button(settings_frame, text="Generate Move List", command=self.process_file).pack(side=tk.RIGHT)

        # Results
        self.text_display = tk.Text(main_frame, wrap=tk.NONE, font=("Consolas", 10))
        vs = ttk.Scrollbar(main_frame, orient=tk.VERTICAL, command=self.text_display.yview)
        hs = ttk.Scrollbar(main_frame, orient=tk.HORIZONTAL, command=self.text_display.xview)
        self.text_display.configure(yscrollcommand=vs.set, xscrollcommand=hs.set)

        ttk.Button(main_frame, text="Save to File", command=self.save_results).pack(side=tk.BOTTOM, pady=5)
        vs.pack(side=tk.RIGHT, fill=tk.Y); hs.pack(side=tk.BOTTOM, fill=tk.X)
        self.text_display.pack(side=tk.LEFT, fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True)

    def browse_file(self):
        fn = filedialog.askopenfilename(filetypes=[("XML files", "*.xml"), ("All files", "*.*")])
        if fn: self.file_path.set(fn)

    def process_file(self):
        if not self.file_path.get(): return messagebox.showerror("Error", "Select a file.")
        
        try:
            tree = ET.parse(self.file_path.get())
            root = tree.getroot()
            data = [[c.text for c in item.findall("Cell/Data")] for item in root.findall(".//Row")]
            
            # Map columns based on your specific SAP export layout
            df = pd.DataFrame([d for d in data if d], columns=['Material', 'Bin', 'Qty', 'Capacity'])
            df['Qty'] = pd.to_numeric(df['Qty'], errors='coerce').fillna(0)
            df['Capacity'] = pd.to_numeric(df['Capacity'], errors='coerce').fillna(100)
            
            # Dynamically identify Rows and Bin Numbers
            norm_results = df['Bin'].apply(normalize_bin)
            df['Row'] = norm_results.apply(lambda x: x[0])
            df['BinNum'] = norm_results.apply(lambda x: x[1])

            moves = []
            thresh = self.threshold.get()

            # Iterate through every unique Row identified in the data
            for (mat, row_id), group in df.groupby(['Material', 'Row']):
                if row_id is None: continue
                
                targets = group[group['BinNum'] < thresh].sort_values('BinNum').to_dict('records')
                sources = group[group['BinNum'] >= thresh].sort_values('BinNum', ascending=False).to_dict('records')

                for src in sources:
                    for tgt in targets:
                        space = tgt['Capacity'] - tgt['Qty']
                        if space > 0 and src['Qty'] > 0:
                            qty = min(space, src['Qty'])
                            moves.append(f"[{row_id}] MOVE {qty} of {mat}: Bin {src['Bin']} -> Bin {tgt['Bin']}")
                            src['Qty'] -= qty; tgt['Qty'] += qty

            self.text_display.delete('1.0', tk.END)
            self.text_display.insert(tk.END, "\n".join(moves) if moves else "No consolidation moves found.")
            
        except Exception as e:
            messagebox.showerror("Error", f"Failed to process: {e}")

    def save_results(self):
        txt = self.text_display.get('1.0', tk.END)
        if txt.strip():
            f = filedialog.asksaveasfile(defaultextension=".txt")
            if f: f.write(txt); f.close()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    root = tk.Tk()
    ConsolidatorApp(root)
    root.mainloop()

Yep. Here’s a **complete** `C:\temp\consolidator_gui.py` that:
