```powershell
# Create folder if it doesn't exist
mkdir C:\temp -Force | Out-Null

@'
import re
import pandas as pd
import xml.etree.ElementTree as ET
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import filedialog, messagebox, ttk

def normalize_bin(bin_name: str):
    """
    Dynamic bin parser:
      '2A33' -> row='A',  num=33,  norm='A33'
      'AA07' -> row='AA', num=7,   norm='AA07'
      'R1'   -> row='R',  num=1,   norm='R01'
    Returns (row_id, bin_num, normalized_bin_string).
    If it doesn't match letters+digits, returns (None, None, original).
    """
    s = str(bin_name).strip()
    m = re.match(r'^(\d+)?([A-Za-z]+)(\d+)$', s)
    if not m:
        return None, None, s
    row_id = m.group(2).upper()
    num = int(m.group(3))
    # 2-digit padding (change to :03d if your warehouse uses 001-999)
    return row_id, num, f"{row_id}{num:02d}"

def parse_sap_snapshot_xml(path: str) -> pd.DataFrame:
    """
    Parses SAP SpreadsheetML XML where the table lines are pipe-delimited in ss:Data.
    Expected columns (by the existing export you provided earlier):
      Bin = parts[6], Material = parts[7], Description = parts[8],
      Stock = parts[11], Capacity = parts[17] (if present)
    """
    tree = ET.parse(path)
    root = tree.getroot()
    ns = {"ss": "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet"}

    rows = []
    for data_node in root.findall(".//ss:Data", ns):
        text = data_node.text or ""
        for line in text.split("\n"):
            if not line.startswith("|"):
                continue
            if "StorageBin" in line or "---" in line:
                continue

            parts = [p.strip() for p in line.split("|")]
            if len(parts) <= 11:
                continue

            try:
                raw_bin = parts[6]
                material = parts[7]
                desc = parts[8]
                stock = float(parts[11].replace(",", "")) if parts[11] else 0.0
                cap = float(parts[17].replace(",", "")) if len(parts) > 17 and parts[17] else 0.0
            except Exception:
                continue

            row_id, bin_num, norm_bin = normalize_bin(raw_bin)

            # Only include bins that we can interpret (letters+digits)
            if bin_num is None:
                continue

            rows.append({
                "Material": material,
                "BinRaw": raw_bin,
                "Bin": norm_bin,
                "Row": row_id,
                "BinNum": int(bin_num),
                "Qty": float(stock),
                "Capacity": float(cap),
                "Description": desc
            })

    df = pd.DataFrame(rows)
    return df

def build_moves_across_rows(df: pd.DataFrame, threshold: int):
    """
    Core logic:
      - Bins with BinNum >= threshold are SOURCES (we want them emptied).
      - Bins with BinNum < threshold are TARGETS (we can fill them).
      - Consolidation happens across ALL rows for the same Material.
    """
    moves = []

    for material, group in df.groupby("Material"):
        if len(group) < 2:
            continue

        # SOURCES: near-line bins we want to empty
        sources = group[(group["BinNum"] >= threshold) & (group["Qty"] > 0)].sort_values("BinNum", ascending=False)

        # TARGETS: farther bins we can fill
        targets = group[(group["BinNum"] < threshold) & (group["Qty"] < group["Capacity"])].sort_values("BinNum", ascending=True)

        if sources.empty or targets.empty:
            continue

        tgt_qty = targets["Qty"].to_dict()

        for _, src in sources.iterrows():
            remaining = float(src["Qty"])
            if remaining <= 0:
                continue

            for t_idx in targets.index:
                tgt = targets.loc[t_idx]
                cap = float(tgt["Capacity"])
                curr = float(tgt_qty[t_idx])
                space = cap - curr

                # don't move into full targets
                if space <= 0:
                    continue

                # don't move into bins closer/equal to source number (keeps direction consistent)
                if int(tgt["BinNum"]) >= int(src["BinNum"]):
                    continue

                qty = min(space, remaining)
                if qty <= 0:
                    continue

                moves.append({
                    "Material": material,
                    "From": src["Bin"],
                    "To": tgt["Bin"],
                    "Qty": qty,
                    "Description": src["Description"]
                })

                remaining -= qty
                tgt_qty[t_idx] = curr + qty

                if remaining <= 0:
                    break

    return moves


class ConsolidatorApp:
    def __init__(self, root: tk.Tk) -> None:
        self.root = root
        self.root.title("Consolidator – Warehouse Line Clearance")
        self.root.geometry("980x680")

        self.file_path = tk.StringVar()
        self.threshold = tk.IntVar(value=40)

        self.text_display = None
        self._setup_ui()

    def _setup_ui(self):
        main = ttk.Frame(self.root, padding="10")
        main.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True)

        file_frame = ttk.LabelFrame(main, text="SAP Snapshot (XML)", padding="10")
        file_frame.pack(fill=tk.X, pady=6)

        ttk.Entry(file_frame, textvariable=self.file_path, width=80).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)
        ttk.Button(file_frame, text="Browse", command=self.browse_file).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)

        settings = ttk.Frame(main, padding="6")
        settings.pack(fill=tk.X)

        ttk.Label(settings, text="Keep bins >= threshold EMPTY (sources only):").pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)
        ttk.Spinbox(settings, from_=1, to=999, increment=1, textvariable=self.threshold, width=6).pack(side=tk.LEFT)

        ttk.Button(settings, text="Generate Move List", command=self.process_file).pack(side=tk.RIGHT, padx=5)
        ttk.Button(settings, text="Save to File", command=self.save_results).pack(side=tk.RIGHT, padx=5)

        # Results box
        box = ttk.LabelFrame(main, text="Moves", padding="10")
        box.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True, pady=6)

        self.text_display = tk.Text(box, wrap=tk.NONE, font=("Consolas", 10))
        vs = ttk.Scrollbar(box, orient=tk.VERTICAL, command=self.text_display.yview)
        hs = ttk.Scrollbar(box, orient=tk.HORIZONTAL, command=self.text_display.xview)
        self.text_display.configure(yscrollcommand=vs.set, xscrollcommand=hs.set)

        self.text_display.pack(side=tk.LEFT, fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True)
        vs.pack(side=tk.RIGHT, fill=tk.Y)
        hs.pack(side=tk.BOTTOM, fill=tk.X)

    def browse_file(self):
        fn = filedialog.askopenfilename(filetypes=[("XML files", "*.xml"), ("All files", "*.*")])
        if fn:
            self.file_path.set(fn)

    def process_file(self):
        path = self.file_path.get().strip()
        if not path:
            return messagebox.showerror("Error", "Select an XML snapshot file first.")

        try:
            df = parse_sap_snapshot_xml(path)

            if df.empty:
                self._print("No usable bin rows found in this XML.\n"
                            "This tool expects SAP SpreadsheetML exports where rows are pipe-delimited inside ss:Data.")
                return

            # Filter out nonsense bins (optional: remove this if you truly want ANY bin number)
            # Keeping everything that parses as letters+digits already.
            threshold = int(self.threshold.get())

            moves = build_moves_across_rows(df, threshold)

            if not moves:
                self._print("No consolidation moves found.\n"
                            f"Either bins >= {threshold} are already empty, or there is no space in bins < {threshold}.")
                return

            lines = []
            lines.append(f"Found {len(moves)} moves. (Bins >= {threshold} are sources only)\n")
            lines.append(f"{'MATERIAL':<12} | {'FROM':<12} -> {'TO':<12} | {'QTY':>8} | DESCRIPTION")
            lines.append("-" * 95)

            for m in moves:
                lines.append(f"{m['Material']:<12} | {m['From']:<12} -> {m['To']:<12} | {m['Qty']:>8.2f} | {m['Description']}")

            self._print("\n".join(lines))

        except Exception as e:
            messagebox.showerror("Error", f"Failed to process file:\n{e}")

    def _print(self, text: str):
        self.text_display.delete("1.0", tk.END)
        self.text_display.insert(tk.END, text)

    def save_results(self):
        txt = self.text_display.get("1.0", tk.END).strip()
        if not txt:
            return

        f = filedialog.asksaveasfilename(defaultextension=".txt", filetypes=[("Text files", "*.txt"), ("All files", "*.*")])
        if not f:
            return

        try:
            with open(f, "w", encoding="utf-8") as out:
                out.write(txt + "\n")
            messagebox.showinfo("Saved", f"Saved to:\n{f}")
        except Exception as e:
            messagebox.showerror("Error", f"Could not save:\n{e}")


if __name__ == "__main__":
    root = tk.Tk()
    ConsolidatorApp(root)
    root.mainloop()
```

That’s almost always **because your SAP export column order doesn’t match the hard-coded indexes** in the parser (Bin = `parts[6]`, Material = `parts[7]`, Stock = `parts[11]`, Capacity = `parts[17]`). If your report variant has extra columns, missing columns, or different order, the parser will grab the wrong fields and everything shifts (“column 1/3 wrong” vibes).

### Fix it the right way: detect columns by HEADER names (no more brittle indexes)
Change your parser to read the header row (the line containing `StorageBin`, `Material`, etc.) and build a name→index map.

Replace your `parse_sap_snapshot_xml()` with this:

```python
def parse_sap_snapshot_xml(path: str) -> pd.DataFrame:
    tree = ET.parse(path)
    root = tree.getroot()
    ns = {"ss": "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet"}

    col_index = None
    rows = []

    def pick(cols, *names):
        """Return first matching column index for any of the names, or None."""
        if not cols:
            return None
        lookup = {c.strip().lower(): i for i, c in enumerate(cols) if c}
        for n in names:
            i = lookup.get(n.lower())
            if i is not None:
                return i
        return None

    for data_node in root.findall(".//ss:Data", ns):
        text = data_node.text or ""
        for line in text.split("\n"):
            if not line.startswith("|"):
                continue
            parts = [p.strip() for p in line.split("|")]

            # HEADER line: build mapping once
            if any(h in line for h in ["StorageBin", "Material", "TotalStock", "Capacity", "Description"]):
                # Keep only non-empty columns for mapping, but preserve indices
                col_index = {
                    "bin": pick(parts, "StorageBin", "Bin", "Storage Bin"),
                    "mat": pick(parts, "Material", "MaterialNumber", "Product"),
                    "desc": pick(parts, "Description", "Material Description", "Matl Desc"),
                    "stock": pick(parts, "TotalStock", "Stock", "Qty", "Quantity", "Total Stock"),
                    "cap": pick(parts, "Capacity", "MaxStock", "Max Stock", "Cap", "MaxQty"),
                }
                continue

            # Data rows
            if col_index is None:
                continue  # haven’t seen header yet

            try:
                raw_bin = parts[col_index["bin"]] if col_index["bin"] is not None else ""
                material = parts[col_index["mat"]] if col_index["mat"] is not None else ""
                desc = parts[col_index["desc"]] if col_index["desc"] is not None else ""
                stock_s = parts[col_index["stock"]] if col_index["stock"] is not None else "0"
                cap_s = parts[col_index["cap"]] if col_index["cap"] is not None else "0"

                stock = float(stock_s.replace(",", "")) if stock_s else 0.0
                cap = float(cap_s.replace(",", "")) if cap_s else 0.0
            except Exception:
                continue

            row_id, bin_num, norm_bin = normalize_bin(raw_bin)
            if bin_num is None:
                continue

            rows.append({
                "Material": material,
                "BinRaw": raw_bin,
                "Bin": norm_bin,
                "Row": row_id,
                "BinNum": int(bin_num),
                "Qty": stock,
                "Capacity": cap,
                "Description": desc
            })

    return pd.DataFrame(rows)
```

### Why this fixes your “column 1/3” issue
Because it **stops assuming** column positions and instead keys off whatever your export calls the columns.

## Do this: replace your parser with header-mapping (works with your bins.xml)

Open your `C:\temp\consolidator_gui.py` and replace your `parse_sap_snapshot_xml()` with the version below (or just overwrite the whole file using the PowerShell block further down).

### Drop-in replacement function
```python
def parse_sap_snapshot_xml(path: str) -> pd.DataFrame:
    tree = ET.parse(path)
    root = tree.getroot()
    ns = {"ss": "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet"}

    header_map = None
    rows = []

    def build_header_map(parts):
        # map lowercased header -> index
        idx = {p.strip().lower(): i for i, p in enumerate(parts) if p and p.strip()}
        def pick(*names):
            for n in names:
                i = idx.get(n.lower())
                if i is not None:
                    return i
            return None

        return {
            "bin":  pick("StorageBin", "Storage Bin", "Bin"),
            "mat":  pick("Materia", "Material", "Product"),
            "desc": pick("Material Description", "Description", "Matl Desc"),
            "stock":pick("Total Stock", "TotalStock", "Stock", "Avail.stock", "Qty", "Quantity"),
            "cap":  pick("Total capacity", "Capacity", "Cap", "Max Stock", "MaxStock"),
        }

    # SAP lines are pipe-delimited inside ss:Data
    for data_node in root.findall(".//ss:Data", ns):
        text = data_node.text or ""
        for line in text.split("\n"):
            if not line.startswith("|"):
                continue
            if "---" in line:
                continue

            parts = [p.strip() for p in line.split("|")]

            # Detect header
            if ("storagebin" in line.lower()) and (("total stock" in line.lower()) or ("avail.stock" in line.lower())):
                header_map = build_header_map(parts)
                continue

            if header_map is None:
                continue  # haven’t seen header yet

            try:
                i_bin = header_map["bin"]
                i_mat = header_map["mat"]
                i_desc = header_map["desc"]
                i_stock = header_map["stock"]
                i_cap = header_map["cap"]

                if None in (i_bin, i_mat, i_stock, i_cap):
                    continue

                raw_bin = parts[i_bin]
                material = parts[i_mat]
                desc = parts[i_desc] if i_desc is not None and i_desc < len(parts) else ""
                stock_s = parts[i_stock] if i_stock < len(parts) else "0"
                cap_s = parts[i_cap] if i_cap < len(parts) else "0"

                stock = float(stock_s.replace(",", "")) if stock_s else 0.0
                cap = float(cap_s.replace(",", "")) if cap_s else 0.0
            except Exception:
                continue

            row_id, bin_num, norm_bin = normalize_bin(raw_bin)
            if bin_num is None:
                continue

            rows.append({
                "Material": material,
                "BinRaw": raw_bin,
                "Bin": norm_bin,
                "Row": row_id,
                "BinNum": int(bin_num),
                "Qty": stock,
                "Capacity": cap,
                "Description": desc
            })

    return pd.DataFrame(rows)
```

code = r'''
import os
import re
import pandas as pd
import xml.etree.ElementTree as ET
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import filedialog, messagebox, ttk

def normalize_bin(bin_name: str):
    """
    Dynamic bin parser (supports any row letters):
      '2A33'  -> row='A',  num=33, norm='A33'
      'AA07'  -> row='AA', num=7,  norm='AA07'
      'R1'    -> row='R',  num=1,  norm='R01'
    Returns (row_id, bin_num, normalized_bin_string). If not match, returns (None, None, original).
    """
    s = str(bin_name).strip()
    m = re.match(r'^(\d+)?([A-Za-z]+)(\d+)$', s)
    if not m:
        return None, None, s
    row_id = m.group(2).upper()
    num = int(m.group(3))
    return row_id, num, f"{row_id}{num:02d}"

def _find_col(cols, candidates):
    """Case-insensitive column finder with light normalization."""
    norm = {}
    for c in cols:
        if c is None:
            continue
        key = re.sub(r'\s+', ' ', str(c).strip().lower())
        norm[key] = c
    for cand in candidates:
        ck = re.sub(r'\s+', ' ', cand.strip().lower())
        if ck in norm:
            return norm[ck]
    return None

def parse_snapshot(path: str) -> pd.DataFrame:
    """
    Supports:
      - .xlsx / .xlsm / .xls  (SAP exported spreadsheet)
      - .xml (SpreadsheetML style export with pipe-delimited rows in ss:Data)
    Returns normalized dataframe with: Material, BinRaw, Bin, Row, BinNum, Qty, Capacity, Description
    """
    ext = os.path.splitext(path)[1].lower()

    if ext in (".xlsx", ".xlsm", ".xls"):
        df0 = pd.read_excel(path, sheet_name=0, engine="openpyxl")
        # Drop completely empty rows
        df0 = df0.dropna(how="all")

        cols = list(df0.columns)

        col_bin = _find_col(cols, ["Storage Bin", "StorageBin", "Storage bin", "Bin"])
        col_mat = _find_col(cols, ["Material", "Materia", "Material Number", "Product"])
        col_desc = _find_col(cols, ["Material Description", "Description", "Matl Desc"])
        col_stock = _find_col(cols, ["Total Stock", "TotalStock", "Available stock", "Avail.stock", "Qty", "Quantity"])
        col_cap = _find_col(cols, ["Total capacity", "Capacity", "Cap", "Max Stock", "MaxStock"])
        # optional if Total capacity missing
        col_rem = _find_col(cols, ["Remaining capacity", "Remain.capacity", "Remain. capacity", "Remaining Capacity"])

        missing = [name for name, col in [("Storage Bin", col_bin), ("Material", col_mat), ("Stock", col_stock)] if col is None]
        if missing:
            raise ValueError(f"Missing required columns in XLSX: {', '.join(missing)}")

        # Build normalized rows
        rows = []
        for _, r in df0.iterrows():
            raw_bin = r.get(col_bin, "")
            material = r.get(col_mat, "")
            if material is None or str(material).strip() == "" or str(material).strip().lower() == "<<empty>>":
                continue

            desc = str(r.get(col_desc, "") or "")
            stock = pd.to_numeric(r.get(col_stock, 0), errors="coerce")
            stock = 0.0 if pd.isna(stock) else float(stock)

            cap = 0.0
            if col_cap is not None:
                capv = pd.to_numeric(r.get(col_cap, 0), errors="coerce")
                cap = 0.0 if pd.isna(capv) else float(capv)

            # If capacity column missing/zero but remaining exists, infer cap = stock + remaining
            if (cap is None or cap == 0.0) and col_rem is not None:
                remv = pd.to_numeric(r.get(col_rem, 0), errors="coerce")
                rem = 0.0 if pd.isna(remv) else float(remv)
                cap = stock + rem

            row_id, bin_num, norm_bin = normalize_bin(raw_bin)
            if bin_num is None:
                continue

            rows.append({
                "Material": str(material).strip(),
                "BinRaw": str(raw_bin).strip(),
                "Bin": norm_bin,
                "Row": row_id,
                "BinNum": int(bin_num),
                "Qty": float(stock),
                "Capacity": float(cap),
                "Description": desc
            })

        return pd.DataFrame(rows)

    # XML: SpreadsheetML with pipe-delimited data in ss:Data
    tree = ET.parse(path)
    root = tree.getroot()
    ns = {"ss": "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet"}

    header_map = None
    rows = []

    def build_header_map(parts):
        idx = {re.sub(r"\s+", " ", (p or "").strip().lower()): i for i, p in enumerate(parts)}
        def pick(*names):
            for n in names:
                k = re.sub(r"\s+", " ", n.strip().lower())
                if k in idx:
                    return idx[k]
            return None
        return {
            "bin":  pick("StorageBin", "Storage Bin", "Bin"),
            "mat":  pick("Material", "Materia", "Product"),
            "desc": pick("Material Description", "Description", "Matl Desc"),
            "stock":pick("Total Stock", "TotalStock", "Available stock", "Avail.stock", "Qty", "Quantity"),
            "cap":  pick("Total capacity", "Capacity", "Cap", "Max Stock", "MaxStock"),
            "rem":  pick("Remaining capacity", "Remain.capacity", "Remain. capacity"),
        }

    for data_node in root.findall(".//ss:Data", ns):
        text = data_node.text or ""
        for line in text.split("\n"):
            if not line.startswith("|"):
                continue
            if "---" in line:
                continue
            parts = [p.strip() for p in line.split("|")]

            # detect header line
            low = line.lower()
            if ("storagebin" in low or "storage bin" in low) and ("material" in low or "materia" in low):
                header_map = build_header_map(parts)
                continue

            if header_map is None:
                continue

            try:
                i_bin = header_map["bin"]
                i_mat = header_map["mat"]
                i_desc = header_map["desc"]
                i_stock = header_map["stock"]
                i_cap = header_map["cap"]
                i_rem = header_map["rem"]

                if i_bin is None or i_mat is None or i_stock is None:
                    continue

                raw_bin = parts[i_bin] if i_bin < len(parts) else ""
                material = parts[i_mat] if i_mat < len(parts) else ""
                if material.strip().lower() == "<<empty>>" or material.strip() == "":
                    continue
                desc = parts[i_desc] if i_desc is not None and i_desc < len(parts) else ""
                stock_s = parts[i_stock] if i_stock < len(parts) else "0"
                stock = float(stock_s.replace(",", "")) if stock_s else 0.0

                cap = 0.0
                if i_cap is not None and i_cap < len(parts):
                    cap_s = parts[i_cap]
                    cap = float(cap_s.replace(",", "")) if cap_s else 0.0
                if (cap == 0.0) and (i_rem is not None) and (i_rem < len(parts)):
                    rem_s = parts[i_rem]
                    rem = float(rem_s.replace(",", "")) if rem_s else 0.0
                    cap = stock + rem
            except Exception:
                continue

            row_id, bin_num, norm_bin = normalize_bin(raw_bin)
            if bin_num is None:
                continue

            rows.append({
                "Material": material,
                "BinRaw": raw_bin,
                "Bin": norm_bin,
                "Row": row_id,
                "BinNum": int(bin_num),
                "Qty": float(stock),
                "Capacity": float(cap),
                "Description": desc
            })

    return pd.DataFrame(rows)

def build_moves_across_rows(df: pd.DataFrame, threshold: int):
    """
    - Sources are bins with BinNum >= threshold (we empty them)
    - Targets are bins with BinNum < threshold and Qty < Capacity
    - Consolidates across ALL rows for the same material
    """
    moves = []
    for material, group in df.groupby("Material"):
        if len(group) < 2:
            continue

        sources = group[(group["BinNum"] >= threshold) & (group["Qty"] > 0)].sort_values("BinNum", ascending=False)
        targets = group[(group["BinNum"] < threshold) & (group["Qty"] < group["Capacity"])].sort_values("BinNum", ascending=True)

        if sources.empty or targets.empty:
            continue

        tgt_qty = targets["Qty"].to_dict()

        for _, src in sources.iterrows():
            remaining = float(src["Qty"])
            if remaining <= 0:
                continue

            for t_idx in targets.index:
                tgt = targets.loc[t_idx]
                if int(tgt["BinNum"]) >= int(src["BinNum"]):
                    continue
                cap = float(tgt["Capacity"])
                curr = float(tgt_qty[t_idx])
                space = cap - curr
                if space <= 0:
                    continue

                qty = min(space, remaining)
                if qty <= 0:
                    continue

                moves.append({
                    "Material": material,
                    "From": src["Bin"],
                    "To": tgt["Bin"],
                    "Qty": qty,
                    "Description": src["Description"]
                })

                remaining -= qty
                tgt_qty[t_idx] = curr + qty
                if remaining <= 0:
                    break
    return moves

class ConsolidatorApp:
    def __init__(self, root: tk.Tk) -> None:
        self.root = root
        self.root.title("Consolidator – Warehouse Line Clearance")
        self.root.geometry("1020x700")

        self.file_path = tk.StringVar()
        self.threshold = tk.IntVar(value=40)

        self.moves_cache = []  # keep latest moves for saving as CSV
        self.text_display = None

        self._setup_ui()

    def _setup_ui(self):
        main = ttk.Frame(self.root, padding="10")
        main.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True)

        file_frame = ttk.LabelFrame(main, text="SAP Export (XML or XLSX)", padding="10")
        file_frame.pack(fill=tk.X, pady=6)

        ttk.Entry(file_frame, textvariable=self.file_path, width=85).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)
        ttk.Button(file_frame, text="Browse", command=self.browse_file).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)

        settings = ttk.Frame(main, padding="6")
        settings.pack(fill=tk.X)

        ttk.Label(settings, text="Keep bins >= threshold EMPTY (sources only):").pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)
        ttk.Spinbox(settings, from_=1, to=999, increment=1, textvariable=self.threshold, width=6).pack(side=tk.LEFT)

        ttk.Button(settings, text="Generate Move List", command=self.process_file).pack(side=tk.RIGHT, padx=5)
        ttk.Button(settings, text="Save (TXT/CSV)", command=self.save_results).pack(side=tk.RIGHT, padx=5)

        box = ttk.LabelFrame(main, text="Moves", padding="10")
        box.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True, pady=6)

        self.text_display = tk.Text(box, wrap=tk.NONE, font=("Consolas", 10))
        vs = ttk.Scrollbar(box, orient=tk.VERTICAL, command=self.text_display.yview)
        hs = ttk.Scrollbar(box, orient=tk.HORIZONTAL, command=self.text_display.xview)
        self.text_display.configure(yscrollcommand=vs.set, xscrollcommand=hs.set)

        self.text_display.pack(side=tk.LEFT, fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True)
        vs.pack(side=tk.RIGHT, fill=tk.Y)
        hs.pack(side=tk.BOTTOM, fill=tk.X)

    def browse_file(self):
        fn = filedialog.askopenfilename(
            filetypes=[("SAP exports", "*.xlsx *.xlsm *.xml *.xls"), ("All files", "*.*")]
        )
        if fn:
            self.file_path.set(fn)

    def process_file(self):
        path = self.file_path.get().strip()
        if not path:
            return messagebox.showerror("Error", "Select an export file first.")

        try:
            df = parse_snapshot(path)
            if df.empty:
                self._print("No usable rows were parsed.\n\n"
                            "If this is an XLSX export, it must contain columns like:\n"
                            "  Storage Bin, Material, Total Stock, Total capacity\n\n"
                            "If this is an XML export, it must be SpreadsheetML with pipe-delimited rows.")
                self.moves_cache = []
                return

            threshold = int(self.threshold.get())
            moves = build_moves_across_rows(df, threshold)
            self.moves_cache = moves

            if not moves:
                self._print(f"No consolidation moves found.\n\n"
                            f"Either bins >= {threshold} are already empty, or there is no space in bins < {threshold}.")
                return

            unique_rows = sorted({r for r in df["Row"].dropna().unique()})
            header = []
            header.append(f"Parsed {len(df)} bin rows | Materials: {df['Material'].nunique()} | Row IDs seen: {', '.join(unique_rows[:30])}{'...' if len(unique_rows)>30 else ''}")
            header.append(f"Found {len(moves)} moves. (Bins >= {threshold} are sources only)\n")
            header.append(f"{'MATERIAL':<12} | {'FROM':<12} -> {'TO':<12} | {'QTY':>8} | DESCRIPTION")
            header.append("-" * 105)

            lines = header
            for m in moves:
                lines.append(f"{m['Material']:<12} | {m['From']:<12} -> {m['To']:<12} | {m['Qty']:>8.2f} | {m['Description']}")

            self._print("\n".join(lines))

        except Exception as e:
            messagebox.showerror("Error", f"Failed to process file:\n{e}")

    def _print(self, text: str):
        self.text_display.delete("1.0", tk.END)
        self.text_display.insert(tk.END, text)

    def save_results(self):
        txt = self.text_display.get("1.0", tk.END).strip()
        if not txt:
            return

        f = filedialog.asksaveasfilename(
            defaultextension=".txt",
            filetypes=[("Text files", "*.txt"), ("CSV files", "*.csv"), ("All files", "*.*")]
        )
        if not f:
            return

        try:
            if f.lower().endswith(".csv"):
                # Write structured CSV from cached moves
                df = pd.DataFrame(self.moves_cache)
                if df.empty:
                    # fallback to raw text
                    with open(f, "w", encoding="utf-8") as out:
                        out.write(txt + "\n")
                else:
                    df.to_csv(f, index=False)
            else:
                with open(f, "w", encoding="utf-8") as out:
                    out.write(txt + "\n")
            messagebox.showinfo("Saved", f"Saved to:\n{f}")
        except Exception as e:
            messagebox.showerror("Error", f"Could not save:\n{e}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    root = tk.Tk()
    ConsolidatorApp(root)
    root.mainloop()

[ASSISTANT]
Good, this explains the problem exactly. 👍  
Your **new upload is `EXPORT.XLSX`**, not the SAP **SpreadsheetML XML** you were using before.

So what’s happening is **not a logic bug** — it’s a **file-format mismatch**.

---

## What changed (the real issue)

Your current app **only knows how to read SAP SpreadsheetML XML**, where data lives inside:

```
<ss:Data> | col | col | col | </ss:Data>
```

But **`EXPORT.XLSX` is a real Excel workbook**, not XML text with pipes.

So when you load it:
- there are **no `|` lines**
- no `<ss:Data>`
- no header row inside text
→ the parser finds **nothing**, or columns shift and look “wrong (column 1 / 3)”

This is 100% expected behavior.

---

## You have two clean options (pick one)

### ✅ OPTION A — Support BOTH XML *and* XLSX (recommended)
We make the app **auto-detect the file type**:
- `.xml` → use SAP XML parser
- `.xlsx` → use pandas Excel reader

This makes the tool future-proof and shift-proof.

### ❌ OPTION B — Force XML only
You keep exporting **XML only** from SAP and never use XLSX.  
(Works, but brittle and annoying.)

You clearly want **Option A**.

---

## The fix: add XLSX support (drop-in, safe)

### 1️⃣ Add this function to `consolidator_gui.py`

```python
def parse_excel_snapshot_xlsx(path: str) -> pd.DataFrame:
    df = pd.read_excel(path)

    # Normalize column names
    cols = {c.lower().strip(): c for c in df.columns}

    def pick(*names):
        for n in names:
            for k, v in cols.items():
                if n.lower() in k:
                    return v
        return None

    col_bin   = pick("storagebin", "storage bin", "bin")
    col_mat   = pick("material", "product", "materia")
    col_desc  = pick("description", "material description")
    col_stock = pick("total stock", "stock", "qty", "quantity")
    col_cap   = pick("capacity", "total capacity", "max")

    if not all([col_bin, col_mat, col_stock]):
        raise ValueError("Required columns not found in XLSX")

    rows = []
    for _, r in df.iterrows():
        raw_bin = str(r[col_bin]).strip()
        material = str(r[col_mat]).strip()
        desc = str(r[col_desc]) if col_desc else ""
        stock = float(r[col_stock]) if pd.notna(r[col_stock]) else 0.0
        cap = float(r[col_cap]) if col_cap and pd.notna(r[col_cap]) else 0.0

        row_id, bin_num, norm_bin = normalize_bin(raw_bin)
        if bin_num is None:
            continue

        rows.append({
            "Material": material,
            "BinRaw": raw_bin,
            "Bin": norm_bin,
            "Row": row_id,
            "BinNum": int(bin_num),
            "Qty": stock,
            "Capacity": cap,
            "Description": desc,
        })

    return pd.DataFrame(rows)
```

You keep getting **.XLSX** because you’re exporting through a path that defaults to **Office Open XML** (xlsx) — that’s the “spreadsheet export” behavior in a lot of SAP screens, especially anything UI5/Fiori-ish (it’s literally designed to export xlsx). citeturn0search12

To get the **XML** your old parser was expecting (Excel 2003 XML / SpreadsheetML), you need to export from an **SAP GUI list/ALV** and **pick the XML format** in the “Select Spreadsheet” dialog. SAP’s own docs describe the flow: *List → Export → Spreadsheet* → choose a format. citeturn0search1turn0search6

## How to export XML from SAP (SAP GUI / ALV)
1. Run your report (LS24 etc.) so the list/grid is on screen.
2. Use one of these:
   - Menu: **List → Export → Spreadsheet** citeturn0search6  
   - Or the **Export** button / spreadsheet icon (depends on your SAP GUI theme).
3. When **Select Spreadsheet** pops up, choose a format like:
   - **“Spreadsheet (XML)”**
   - **“Office 2003 XML”**
   - **“Excel 2003 XML”**
4. Save it locally. You should end up with a `.xml` file.

## Why you might *not* be seeing the XML option anymore
### You previously clicked “Always use selected format”
If you ever chose XLSX and checked “always use selected format”, SAP will stop asking and will keep spitting out xlsx. SAP Community users run into exactly this. citeturn0search2

Fix: export again and **change the format**, and **do not** lock it to always use that one.

### Reset the export-format memory (SAP GUI trick)
Some SAP GUI installs let you reset the remembered Excel/export settings by typing this in the SAP command box while you’re on a report screen:

```
&reset_excel
```

That resets the file export options back to default. citeturn0search22

## If you’re exporting from Fiori/WebGUI
Many Fiori/UI5 “Export to Spreadsheet” features output **xlsx only** by design. citeturn0search12  
In that case, you won’t reliably get SpreadsheetML XML from that screen — use SAP GUI export instead.

```powershell
@'
import os
import re
import pandas as pd
import xml.etree.ElementTree as ET
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import filedialog, messagebox, ttk

def normalize_bin(bin_name: str):
    """
    Dynamic bin parser (supports any row letters):
      '2A33'  -> row='A',  num=33, norm='A33'
      'AA07'  -> row='AA', num=7,  norm='AA07'
      'R1'    -> row='R',  num=1,  norm='R01'
    Returns (row_id, bin_num, normalized_bin_string). If not match, returns (None, None, original).
    """
    s = str(bin_name).strip()
    m = re.match(r'^(\d+)?([A-Za-z]+)(\d+)$', s)
    if not m:
        return None, None, s
    row_id = m.group(2).upper()
    num = int(m.group(3))
    return row_id, num, f"{row_id}{num:02d}"


def _find_col(cols, candidates):
    """Case-insensitive column finder with light normalization."""
    norm = {}
    for c in cols:
        if c is None:
            continue
        key = re.sub(r'\s+', ' ', str(c).strip().lower())
        norm[key] = c
    for cand in candidates:
        ck = re.sub(r'\s+', ' ', cand.strip().lower())
        if ck in norm:
            return norm[ck]
    return None


def parse_snapshot(path: str) -> pd.DataFrame:
    """
    Supports:
      - .xlsx / .xlsm / .xls  (SAP exported spreadsheet)
      - .xml (SpreadsheetML style export with pipe-delimited rows in ss:Data)
    Returns normalized dataframe with: Material, BinRaw, Bin, Row, BinNum, Qty, Capacity, Description
    """
    ext = os.path.splitext(path)[1].lower()

    # ===== XLSX / XLSM / XLS =====
    if ext in (".xlsx", ".xlsm", ".xls"):
        df0 = pd.read_excel(path, sheet_name=0, engine="openpyxl")
        df0 = df0.dropna(how="all")

        cols = list(df0.columns)

        col_bin = _find_col(cols, ["Storage Bin", "StorageBin", "Storage bin", "Bin"])
        col_mat = _find_col(cols, ["Material", "Materia", "Material Number", "Product"])
        col_desc = _find_col(cols, ["Material Description", "Description", "Matl Desc"])
        col_stock = _find_col(cols, ["Total Stock", "TotalStock", "Available stock", "Avail.stock", "Qty", "Quantity"])
        col_cap = _find_col(cols, ["Total capacity", "Capacity", "Cap", "Max Stock", "MaxStock"])
        col_rem = _find_col(cols, ["Remaining capacity", "Remain.capacity", "Remain. capacity", "Remaining Capacity"])

        missing = [name for name, col in [("Storage Bin", col_bin), ("Material", col_mat), ("Stock", col_stock)] if col is None]
        if missing:
            raise ValueError(f"Missing required columns in XLSX: {', '.join(missing)}")

        rows = []
        for _, r in df0.iterrows():
            raw_bin = r.get(col_bin, "")
            material = r.get(col_mat, "")

            if material is None or str(material).strip() == "" or str(material).strip().lower() == "<<empty>>":
                continue

            desc = str(r.get(col_desc, "") or "")
            stock = pd.to_numeric(r.get(col_stock, 0), errors="coerce")
            stock = 0.0 if pd.isna(stock) else float(stock)

            cap = 0.0
            if col_cap is not None:
                capv = pd.to_numeric(r.get(col_cap, 0), errors="coerce")
                cap = 0.0 if pd.isna(capv) else float(capv)

            # If cap missing/zero but remaining exists, infer cap = stock + remaining
            if (cap is None or cap == 0.0) and col_rem is not None:
                remv = pd.to_numeric(r.get(col_rem, 0), errors="coerce")
                rem = 0.0 if pd.isna(remv) else float(remv)
                cap = stock + rem

            row_id, bin_num, norm_bin = normalize_bin(raw_bin)
            if bin_num is None:
                continue

            rows.append({
                "Material": str(material).strip(),
                "BinRaw": str(raw_bin).strip(),
                "Bin": norm_bin,
                "Row": row_id,
                "BinNum": int(bin_num),
                "Qty": float(stock),
                "Capacity": float(cap),
                "Description": desc
            })

        return pd.DataFrame(rows)

    # ===== XML (SpreadsheetML) =====
    tree = ET.parse(path)
    root = tree.getroot()
    ns = {"ss": "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet"}

    header_map = None
    rows = []

    def build_header_map(parts):
        idx = {re.sub(r"\s+", " ", (p or "").strip().lower()): i for i, p in enumerate(parts)}
        def pick(*names):
            for n in names:
                k = re.sub(r"\s+", " ", n.strip().lower())
                if k in idx:
                    return idx[k]
            return None
        return {
            "bin":  pick("StorageBin", "Storage Bin", "Bin"),
            "mat":  pick("Material", "Materia", "Product"),
            "desc": pick("Material Description", "Description", "Matl Desc"),
            "stock":pick("Total Stock", "TotalStock", "Available stock", "Avail.stock", "Qty", "Quantity"),
            "cap":  pick("Total capacity", "Capacity", "Cap", "Max Stock", "MaxStock"),
            "rem":  pick("Remaining capacity", "Remain.capacity", "Remain. capacity"),
        }

    for data_node in root.findall(".//ss:Data", ns):
        text = data_node.text or ""
        for line in text.split("\n"):
            if not line.startswith("|"):
                continue
            if "---" in line:
                continue
            parts = [p.strip() for p in line.split("|")]

            low = line.lower()
            if ("storagebin" in low or "storage bin" in low) and ("material" in low or "materia" in low):
                header_map = build_header_map(parts)
                continue

            if header_map is None:
                continue

            try:
                i_bin = header_map["bin"]
                i_mat = header_map["mat"]
                i_desc = header_map["desc"]
                i_stock = header_map["stock"]
                i_cap = header_map["cap"]
                i_rem = header_map["rem"]

                if i_bin is None or i_mat is None or i_stock is None:
                    continue

                raw_bin = parts[i_bin] if i_bin < len(parts) else ""
                material = parts[i_mat] if i_mat < len(parts) else ""
                if material.strip().lower() == "<<empty>>" or material.strip() == "":
                    continue

                desc = parts[i_desc] if i_desc is not None and i_desc < len(parts) else ""
                stock_s = parts[i_stock] if i_stock < len(parts) else "0"
                stock = float(stock_s.replace(",", "")) if stock_s else 0.0

                cap = 0.0
                if i_cap is not None and i_cap < len(parts):
                    cap_s = parts[i_cap]
                    cap = float(cap_s.replace(",", "")) if cap_s else 0.0
                if (cap == 0.0) and (i_rem is not None) and (i_rem < len(parts)):
                    rem_s = parts[i_rem]
                    rem = float(rem_s.replace(",", "")) if rem_s else 0.0
                    cap = stock + rem
            except Exception:
                continue

            row_id, bin_num, norm_bin = normalize_bin(raw_bin)
            if bin_num is None:
                continue

            rows.append({
                "Material": material,
                "BinRaw": raw_bin,
                "Bin": norm_bin,
                "Row": row_id,
                "BinNum": int(bin_num),
                "Qty": float(stock),
                "Capacity": float(cap),
                "Description": desc
            })

    return pd.DataFrame(rows)


def build_moves_across_rows(df: pd.DataFrame, threshold: int):
    """
    - Sources are bins with BinNum >= threshold (we empty them)
    - Targets are bins with BinNum < threshold and Qty < Capacity
    - Consolidates across ALL rows for the same material
    """
    moves = []
    for material, group in df.groupby("Material"):
        if len(group) < 2:
            continue

        sources = group[(group["BinNum"] >= threshold) & (group["Qty"] > 0)].sort_values("BinNum", ascending=False)
        targets = group[(group["BinNum"] < threshold) & (group["Qty"] < group["Capacity"])].sort_values("BinNum", ascending=True)

        if sources.empty or targets.empty:
            continue

        tgt_qty = targets["Qty"].to_dict()

        for _, src in sources.iterrows():
            remaining = float(src["Qty"])
            if remaining <= 0:
                continue

            for t_idx in targets.index:
                tgt = targets.loc[t_idx]
                if int(tgt["BinNum"]) >= int(src["BinNum"]):
                    continue

                cap = float(tgt["Capacity"])
                curr = float(tgt_qty[t_idx])
                space = cap - curr
                if space <= 0:
                    continue

                qty = min(space, remaining)
                if qty <= 0:
                    continue

                moves.append({
                    "Material": material,
                    "From": src["Bin"],
                    "To": tgt["Bin"],
                    "Qty": qty,
                    "Description": src["Description"]
                })

                remaining -= qty
                tgt_qty[t_idx] = curr + qty
                if remaining <= 0:
                    break

    return moves


class ConsolidatorApp:
    def __init__(self, root: tk.Tk) -> None:
        self.root = root
        self.root.title("Consolidator – Warehouse Line Clearance")
        self.root.geometry("1020x700")

        self.file_path = tk.StringVar()
        self.threshold = tk.IntVar(value=40)

        self.moves_cache = []  # used for CSV save
        self.text_display = None

        self._setup_ui()

    def _setup_ui(self):
        main = ttk.Frame(self.root, padding="10")
        main.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True)

        file_frame = ttk.LabelFrame(main, text="SAP Export (XLSX or XML)", padding="10")
        file_frame.pack(fill=tk.X, pady=6)

        ttk.Entry(file_frame, textvariable=self.file_path, width=85).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)
        ttk.Button(file_frame, text="Browse", command=self.browse_file).pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)

        settings = ttk.Frame(main, padding="6")
        settings.pack(fill=tk.X)

        ttk.Label(settings, text="Keep bins >= threshold EMPTY (sources only):").pack(side=tk.LEFT, padx=5)
        ttk.Spinbox(settings, from_=1, to=999, increment=1, textvariable=self.threshold, width=6).pack(side=tk.LEFT)

        ttk.Button(settings, text="Generate Move List", command=self.process_file).pack(side=tk.RIGHT, padx=5)
        ttk.Button(settings, text="Save (TXT/CSV)", command=self.save_results).pack(side=tk.RIGHT, padx=5)

        box = ttk.LabelFrame(main, text="Moves", padding="10")
        box.pack(fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True, pady=6)

        self.text_display = tk.Text(box, wrap=tk.NONE, font=("Consolas", 10))
        vs = ttk.Scrollbar(box, orient=tk.VERTICAL, command=self.text_display.yview)
        hs = ttk.Scrollbar(box, orient=tk.HORIZONTAL, command=self.text_display.xview)
        self.text_display.configure(yscrollcommand=vs.set, xscrollcommand=hs.set)

        self.text_display.pack(side=tk.LEFT, fill=tk.BOTH, expand=True)
        vs.pack(side=tk.RIGHT, fill=tk.Y)
        hs.pack(side=tk.BOTTOM, fill=tk.X)

    def browse_file(self):
        fn = filedialog.askopenfilename(
            filetypes=[("SAP exports", "*.xlsx *.xlsm *.xml *.xls"), ("All files", "*.*")]
        )
        if fn:
            self.file_path.set(fn)

    def process_file(self):
        path = self.file_path.get().strip()
        if not path:
            return messagebox.showerror("Error", "Select an export file first.")

        try:
            df = parse_snapshot(path)

            if df.empty:
                self._print(
                    "No usable rows were parsed.\n\n"
                    "For XLSX exports, headers must include at least:\n"
                    "  Storage Bin, Material, Total Stock (or Available stock)\n"
                    "And ideally:\n"
                    "  Total capacity (or Remaining capacity)\n"
                )
                self.moves_cache = []
                return

            threshold = int(self.threshold.get())
            moves = build_moves_across_rows(df, threshold)
            self.moves_cache = moves

            if not moves:
                self._print(
                    f"No consolidation moves found.\n\n"
                    f"Either bins >= {threshold} are already empty, or there is no space in bins < {threshold}."
                )
                return

            unique_rows = sorted({r for r in df["Row"].dropna().unique()})
            lines = []
            lines.append(
                f"Parsed {len(df)} bin rows | Materials: {df['Material'].nunique()} | Row IDs seen: "
                + (", ".join(unique_rows[:30]) + ("..." if len(unique_rows) > 30 else ""))
            )
            lines.append(f"Found {len(moves)} moves. (Bins >= {threshold} are sources only)\n")
            lines.append(f"{'MATERIAL':<12} | {'FROM':<12} -> {'TO':<12} | {'QTY':>8} | DESCRIPTION")
            lines.append("-" * 105)

            for m in moves:
                lines.append(
                    f"{m['Material']:<12} | {m['From']:<12} -> {m['To']:<12} | {m['Qty']:>8.2f} | {m['Description']}"
                )

            self._print("\n".join(lines))

        except Exception as e:
            messagebox.showerror("Error", f"Failed to process file:\n{e}")

    def _print(self, text: str):
        self.text_display.delete("1.0", tk.END)
        self.text_display.insert(tk.END, text)

    def save_results(self):
        txt = self.text_display.get("1.0", tk.END).strip()
        if not txt:
            return

        f = filedialog.asksaveasfilename(
            defaultextension=".txt",
            filetypes=[("Text files", "*.txt"), ("CSV files", "*.csv"), ("All files", "*.*")]
        )
        if not f:
            return

        try:
            if f.lower().endswith(".csv"):
                df = pd.DataFrame(self.moves_cache)
                if df.empty:
                    with open(f, "w", encoding="utf-8") as out:
                        out.write(txt + "\n")
                else:
                    df.to_csv(f, index=False)
            else:
                with open(f, "w", encoding="utf-8") as out:
                    out.write(txt + "\n")

            messagebox.showinfo("Saved", f"Saved to:\n{f}")
        except Exception as e:
            messagebox.showerror("Error", f"Could not save:\n{e}")


if __name__ == "__main__":
    root = tk.Tk()
    ConsolidatorApp(root)
    root.mainloop()
'@ | Set-Content -Path C:\temp\consolidator_gui.py -Encoding UTF8
```

You “locked” the export to XLSX by hitting the **“Always use selected format”** (or equivalent) in SAP’s spreadsheet export dialog. To undo it, you need to **clear SAP GUI’s remembered export choice**.

Here are the practical ways, in order of “works most often”:

## 1) Reset the remembered spreadsheet export (fastest)
In **SAP GUI**, go to the command field (top left) and enter:

```
&RESET_EXCEL
```

Press **Enter**.  
Then run your report again and export — the format chooser should come back so you can pick **XML** instead of XLSX.

*(If your system doesn’t recognize that command, use option 2 or 3 below.)*

## 2) Force the chooser to appear again, then un-check “always”
Do an export again from the same report:
- **List → Export → Spreadsheet**
When the format dialog appears:
- Pick the XML option (Excel 2003 XML / Spreadsheet XML)
- **Make sure the “Always use selected format” box is NOT checked**
- Save

If you don’t see the dialog anymore, SAP is still remembering your default, so do option 3.

## 3) Clear SAP GUI local settings (nuclear option, works)
This resets locally-stored SAP GUI preferences that include export defaults.

1. Close **SAP GUI completely**
2. On Windows, open **Run** (`Win + R`)
3. Run:

```
saplogon.exe
```

Then in SAP Logon:
- Go to **Options**
- Look for **Local Data / Cache / History** settings (varies by SAP GUI version)
- Clear “recently used export settings / history” if present

If you can’t find anything like that, tell me your **SAP GUI version** (Help → About SAP Logon) and I’ll point to the exact spot.

## Do this exactly (SAP GUI)

### 1) Get to an ALV output grid first
Run **any report that shows an ALV grid** (you’ll see a table with column headers, filters/sort, etc.). The reset won’t “take” if you’re not on an ALV list/grid. citeturn0search16turn0search4

Click inside the output grid, then in the command field type:

```
&RESET_EXCEL
```

Press **Enter**.

You should see a status message like **“Setting was deleted”** in the lower-left status bar. citeturn0search16turn0search6turn0search18

> If you don’t see the status message, you were almost certainly not on an ALV grid when you ran it.

### 3) Export again and you should get the format chooser back
Go **List → Export → Spreadsheet**, and the “Select Spreadsheet” dialog should return so you can choose **Spreadsheet (XML) / Excel 2003 XML** (names vary by system). citeturn0search2

## If `&RESET_EXCEL` still doesn’t bring the chooser back

### Option A: Use the right-click “Spreadsheet” trick (often works even when the dialog is locked)
On an ALV grid:
- **Right-click inside the grid** (or the top-left “corner” button of the grid)
- Choose **Spreadsheet**

This often restores the format options immediately. citeturn0search0turn0search1turn0search4turn0search17

### Option B: You’re not in ALV at all (or you’re exporting from a different mechanism)
Some transactions/screens export via a different path and won’t obey ALV’s spreadsheet settings. In those cases, you have to open **any ALV grid report**, reset there, then come back. citeturn0search4turn0search17

### Option C: Last resort (requires BASIS/admin)
If the setting is stuck in the backend SALV/ALV defaults, BASIS can delete your saved export setting using admin utilities (commonly mentioned: `SALV_BS_ADMIN_MAINTAIN`). citeturn0search4

[ASSISTANT]
from openpyxl import load_workbook
from datetime import datetime, date
import xml.sax.saxutils as saxutils
import os, math

xlsx_path = "/mnt/data/EXPORT.XLSX"
out_xml_path = "/mnt/data/EXPORT_spreadsheetml.xml"

wb = load_workbook(xlsx_path, data_only=True)

def ss_type_and_value(v):
    if v is None:
        return None, None
    if isinstance(v, bool):
        return "Boolean", "1" if v else "0"
    if isinstance(v, (int, float)) and not (isinstance(v, float) and (math.isnan(v) or math.isinf(v))):
        return "Number", str(v)
    if isinstance(v, (datetime, date)):
        dt = v if isinstance(v, datetime) else datetime(v.year, v.month, v.day)
        # Excel 2003 XML expects ISO8601 with time
        return "DateTime", dt.strftime("%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S.000")
    # fallback string
    return "String", str(v)

def used_range(ws):
    # openpyxl's max_row/max_column can be big; we shrink by scanning for last non-empty
    max_r = 0
    max_c = 0
    for row in ws.iter_rows(values_only=False):
        r_idx = row[0].row
        row_has = False
        for cell in row:
            if cell.value is not None:
                row_has = True
                max_c = max(max_c, cell.column)
        if row_has:
            max_r = r_idx
    return max_r, max_c

# Build SpreadsheetML 2003
parts = []
parts.append('<?xml version="1.0"?>')
parts.append('<?mso-application progid="Excel.Sheet"?>')
parts.append('<Workbook xmlns="urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet" '
             'xmlns:ss="urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet">')

for ws in wb.worksheets:
    sheet_name = saxutils.escape(ws.title)
    max_r, max_c = used_range(ws)
    parts.append(f'<Worksheet ss:Name="{sheet_name}">')
    parts.append('<Table>')
    if max_r == 0 or max_c == 0:
        # empty sheet
        parts.append('</Table></Worksheet>')
        continue

    for r in range(1, max_r + 1):
        # collect row cells
        row_cells = []
        # find non-empty cells and write with ss:Index skips
        last_written_col = 0
        for c in range(1, max_c + 1):
            v = ws.cell(row=r, column=c).value
            t, val = ss_type_and_value(v)
            if t is None:
                continue
            # If we skipped columns, use ss:Index
            idx_attr = ""
            if c != last_written_col + 1:
                idx_attr = f' ss:Index="{c}"'
            escaped_val = saxutils.escape(val)
            cell_xml = f'<Cell{idx_attr}><Data ss:Type="{t}">{escaped_val}</Data></Cell>'
            row_cells.append(cell_xml)
            last_written_col = c

        if row_cells:
            parts.append('<Row>')
            parts.extend(row_cells)
            parts.append('</Row>')

    parts.append('</Table>')
    parts.append('</Worksheet>')

parts.append('</Workbook>')

with open(out_xml_path, "w", encoding="utf-8") as f:
    f.write("\n".join(parts))

out_xml_path, os.path.getsize(out_xml_path)

[ASSISTANT]
import pandas as pd, math, os
from openpyxl import load_workbook
import xml.sax.saxutils as saxutils

xlsx_path="/mnt/data/EXPORT.XLSX"
out_path="/mnt/data/EXPORT_sap_piped.xml"

# Read first sheet with pandas (preserve headers)
df = pd.read_excel(xlsx_path)

# Helper to find columns by fuzzy name
cols = list(df.columns)
lc = {str(c).strip().lower(): c for c in cols}

def pick_col(*needles):
    for n in needles:
        n = n.lower()
        for c in cols:
            if n in str(c).strip().lower():
                return c
    return None

col_bin = pick_col("storagebin", "storage bin", "bin")
col_mat = pick_col("materia", "material", "product")
col_desc = pick_col("material description", "description", "matl desc", "mat desc")
col_stock = pick_col("total stock", "totalstock", "stock", "qty", "quantity", "avail.stock", "avail stock")
col_cap = pick_col("total capacity", "totalcap", "capacity", "cap", "max stock", "maxstock", "max")

# Build the 17 column positions required by the legacy parser
# 1..17 in cols17 (index in parts after split is same number)
# Place key fields at: 6=bin, 7=material, 8=desc, 11=total stock, 17=capacity
headers17 = [""] * 17
headers17[5] = "StorageBin"
headers17[6] = "Materia"
headers17[7] = "Material Description"
headers17[10] = "Total Stock"
headers17[16] = "Total capacity"

def fmt(v):
    if pd.isna(v) or v is None:
        return ""
    if isinstance(v, float):
        if math.isnan(v) or math.isinf(v):
            return ""
    return str(v)

lines = []
# Header line (parser skips because it contains StorageBin)
lines.append("|" + "|".join([""] + headers17 + [""]) )
# Separator (parser skips because it contains ---)
lines.append("|" + "|".join(["", "---"] + [""]*16 + [""]) )

for _, r in df.iterrows():
    cols17 = [""] * 17
    if col_bin is not None:
        cols17[5] = fmt(r[col_bin])
    if col_mat is not None:
        cols17[6] = fmt(r[col_mat])
    if col_desc is not None:
        cols17[7] = fmt(r[col_desc])
    if col_stock is not None:
        cols17[10] = fmt(r[col_stock])
    if col_cap is not None:
        cols17[16] = fmt(r[col_cap])
    # Skip empty rows (no bin or material)
    if (not cols17[5]) and (not cols17[6]):
        continue
    lines.append("|" + "|".join([""] + cols17 + [""]) )

# Build SpreadsheetML XML with one row per line in a single-cell row
parts=[]
parts.append('<?xml version="1.0"?>')
parts.append('<?mso-application progid="Excel.Sheet"?>')
parts.append('<Workbook xmlns="urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet" '
             'xmlns:ss="urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet">')
parts.append('<Worksheet ss:Name="SAP_EXPORT">')
parts.append('<Table>')

for line in lines:
    parts.append('<Row>')
    parts.append('<Cell><Data ss:Type="String">{}</Data></Cell>'.format(saxutils.escape(line)))
    parts.append('</Row>')

parts.append('</Table>')
parts.append('</Worksheet>')
parts.append('</Workbook>')

with open(out_path,"w",encoding="utf-8") as f:
    f.write("\n".join(parts))

(out_path, os.path.getsize(out_path), {"bin": str(col_bin), "material": str(col_mat), "desc": str(col_desc), "stock": str(col_stock), "cap": str(col_cap)})

[USER]
With all the |||| correct?

[ASSISTANT]
Yes — **with the leading/trailing `|` (“pipes”) per line**, like:

```
| ... | ... | ... |
```

To be precise, for the format your consolidator parser expects:

- **Each row is a single text line** that **starts with `|`**
- Columns are separated by `|`
- It’s fine (and common) to have an **empty field** right after the first pipe (because of `|` + join pattern)
- The header line must include **`StorageBin`** somewhere so the parser can skip/recognize it.

Example (simplified):

```
| |StorageBin|Materia|Material Description|...|Total Stock|...|Total capacity|
| |---|...|
| |A33|285936|WIDGET THING|...|12|...|36|
```

### Important correction
You wrote `||||` (four pipes). You don’t need “exactly four” pipes — you need **pipe-delimited columns** with a leading pipe. The number of pipes depends on how many columns the line has.

### Also
Some earlier files you uploaded expired on my side, so when you send the new version, **upload it again in this chat** and I’ll convert it with the correct pipe structure.

[USER]
What does the exe program ask for

[ASSISTANT]
The **Consolidator.exe** (the GUI one you built from `consolidator_gui.py`) asks for basically two things:

1) **Your SAP export file**  
   - You click **Browse** and pick the snapshot you exported from SAP.  
   - Depending on which script version you built, it expects either:
     - **SAP SpreadsheetML XML** (`.xml`) **OR**
     - **XLSX + XML** (if you added the XLSX-support changes).

2) **A Threshold number** (default was **40**)  
   - Meaning: bins with numbers **≥ threshold** are treated as **near-line bins to EMPTY** (sources only).  
   - Bins with numbers **< threshold** are treated as **targets** to fill up.

Then you click:
- **Generate Move List** → it prints the moves (Material | FromBin → ToBin | Qty | Description)
- **Save to File** → saves the printed results to a `.txt`

That’s it — it doesn’t ask for logins, bin ranges, or anything else unless you added extra fields.

If you want me to tell you *exactly* what **your** current EXE is doing, upload the **exact `consolidator_gui.py` you used to build it** (some earlier uploads expired on my side).

[USER]
The Sap spreadsheetml

[ASSISTANT]
If you’re using the **SAP SpreadsheetML `.xml`** export (the one Excel can open, and SAP GUI sometimes calls “Spreadsheet (XML)” / “Excel 2003 XML”), then **Consolidator.exe asks for only this:**

### 1) The SAP export **XML file**
You click **Browse** and select the `.xml`.

What the program expects to find inside that XML:
- A header row that includes **StorageBin** (or a similar bin header)
- Rows that include, at minimum:
  - **Storage bin**
  - **Material**
  - **Total stock / quantity**
  - **Capacity** (or total capacity)

If the XML is the “piped” style we generated (one cell per row that contains a `| ... |` line), it expects those fields to be in the right positions in the pipe line (Bin, Material, Description, Stock, Capacity).

### 2) A **Threshold number** (default 40)
This tells it what counts as “near the line”:
- bins with numbers **>= threshold** → treated as **sources to empty**
- bins with numbers **< threshold** → treated as **targets to fill**

### Then it outputs:
- A move list: **Material | FromBin → ToBin | Qty | Description**
- And you can **Save to File**.

---

## Common reason it “doesn’t work” with SAP SpreadsheetML
SAP can export **multiple XML “styles”**:
- **True SpreadsheetML grid** (cells in a table)  
- **The weird SAP list dump** where each row is a `| ... |` text line inside `ss:Data`  
Your current parser must match the style you’re feeding it.

If you upload one of your SAP `.xml` files here, I’ll tell you which style it is and whether your current EXE will read it—or what to tweak. (Some older uploads expired, so it needs to be the current file.)

[USER]
How do I convert the xlsx to xml myself?

[ASSISTANT]
You can convert `.xlsx` → `.xml` two totally different ways, depending on what you mean by “XML”:

- **A) Excel 2003 SpreadsheetML XML** (Excel can open it like a workbook)
- **B) “SAP-piped” XML** (the weird one your consolidator parser likes: each row is a single `| ... |` text line inside SpreadsheetML)

I’ll give you both so you’re not stuck.

---

## A) Convert XLSX to normal Excel XML (SpreadsheetML) using Excel
If you have Microsoft Excel on that Surface:

1. Open the `.xlsx` in **Excel**
2. **File → Save As**
3. Choose file type:
   - **“XML Spreadsheet 2003 (*.xml)”** (or similar wording)
4. Save

That produces a legit SpreadsheetML `.xml` file Excel can open again.

If you don’t see that option, jump to the Python method below.

---

## B) Convert XLSX to SAP-style “piped” XML (the one your tool expects)
Excel won’t create this format. You need a tiny Python converter.

### 1) Install the needed Python packages (one time)
Open PowerShell:

```powershell
python -m pip install --upgrade pip pandas openpyxl
```

### 2) Create a converter script
Save this as `C:\temp\xlsx_to_sap_piped_xml.py`

```python
import sys, math
import pandas as pd
import xml.sax.saxutils as saxutils

def pick_col(cols, *needles):
    for n in needles:
        n = n.lower()
        for c in cols:
            if n in str(c).strip().lower():
                return c
    return None

def fmt(v):
    if v is None or (isinstance(v, float) and (math.isnan(v) or math.isinf(v))):
        return ""
    return str(v)

def main(xlsx_path, out_xml_path):
    df = pd.read_excel(xlsx_path)
    cols = list(df.columns)

    col_bin   = pick_col(cols, "storagebin", "storage bin", "bin")
    col_mat   = pick_col(cols, "materia", "material", "product")
    col_desc  = pick_col(cols, "material description", "description", "matl desc", "mat desc")
    col_stock = pick_col(cols, "total stock", "totalstock", "stock", "qty", "quantity", "avail.stock", "avail stock")
    col_cap   = pick_col(cols, "total capacity", "totalcap", "capacity", "cap", "max stock", "maxstock", "max")

    if col_bin is None or col_mat is None or col_stock is None:
        raise SystemExit(f"Missing required columns. Found: {cols}")

    # Build 17-column pipe layout (to match legacy parser expectations)
    headers17 = [""] * 17
    headers17[5]  = "StorageBin"
    headers17[6]  = "Materia"
    headers17[7]  = "Material Description"
    headers17[10] = "Total Stock"
    headers17[16] = "Total capacity"

    lines = []
    lines.append("|" + "|".join([""] + headers17 + [""]))
    lines.append("|" + "|".join(["", "---"] + [""]*16 + [""]))

    for _, r in df.iterrows():
        cols17 = [""] * 17
        cols17[5]  = fmt(r[col_bin])
        cols17[6]  = fmt(r[col_mat])
        cols17[7]  = fmt(r[col_desc]) if col_desc is not None else ""
        cols17[10] = fmt(r[col_stock])
        cols17[16] = fmt(r[col_cap]) if col_cap is not None else ""

        if not cols17[5] and not cols17[6]:
            continue

        lines.append("|" + "|".join([""] + cols17 + [""]))

    # Wrap into SpreadsheetML with one cell per row
    parts = []
    parts.append('<?xml version="1.0"?>')
    parts.append('<?mso-application progid="Excel.Sheet"?>')
    parts.append('<Workbook xmlns="urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet" '
                 'xmlns:ss="urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:spreadsheet">')
    parts.append('<Worksheet ss:Name="SAP_EXPORT"><Table>')

    for line in lines:
        parts.append('<Row><Cell><Data ss:Type="String">{}</Data></Cell></Row>'.format(
            saxutils.escape(line)
        ))

    parts.append('</Table></Worksheet></Workbook>')

    with open(out_xml_path, "w", encoding="utf-8") as f:
        f.write("\n".join(parts))

if __name__ == "__main__":
    if len(sys.argv) != 3:
        raise SystemExit("Usage: python xlsx_to_sap_piped_xml.py input.xlsx output.xml")
    main(sys.argv[1], sys.argv[2])
```

### 3) Run it
```powershell
cd C:\temp
python .\xlsx_to_sap_piped_xml.py .\EXPORT.XLSX .\EXPORT_sap_piped.xml
```

Now you’ve got `EXPORT_sap_piped.xml` in the exact structure your consolidator likes.
