from pathlib import Path

readme = """# Consolidator (Line-Clearance Bin Optimizer)

A Windows desktop tool that reads a SAP warehouse “snapshot” export and generates a **move list** to **clear bins near the line** by moving stock into farther bins where space exists.

This build uses **row-based capacity overrides** because SAP-exported bin capacity is not reliable for your floor layout.

---

## What the program asks for

1) **Input file**: a SAP export (snapshot) in one of these formats:
- **Excel**: `.xlsx` / `.xls`
- **HTML**: `.htm` / `.html` (SAP “Email/HTML” style export)
- **XML**: `.xml` (SpreadsheetML variants and InventoryExport-style XML)

2) **Threshold** (number):
- Bins with **BinNum >= threshold** are treated as **SOURCES** (stuff you want to pull OUT).
- Bins with **BinNum < threshold** are treated as **TARGETS** (bins you want to fill, keeping them near-line).

3) **Row Capacity Overrides** (required):
- The app detects all **Rows** in the file (A, B, C, …, AA, etc.)
- You must choose a capacity **2–45** for **each Row**.
- There are **no defaults**.
- The report **will not run** until every detected Row has a capacity selected.

---

## How it decides moves (current workflow)

For each **Material**:
- **Targets** = bins with `BinNum < threshold` and `Qty < Capacity`
- **Sources** = bins with `BinNum >= threshold` and `Qty > 0`
- It moves stock from **higher BinNum → lower BinNum** until targets are full or sources are empty.

Output is a plain-text report listing:
- Material
- FromBin → ToBin
- Quantity
- Description (if present in export)

---

## Supported file quirks

The parser is designed to survive SAP export differences:
- If column headers differ, it tries **auto-detection** by name and by content.
- If it still can’t tell which column is which, it opens a **column mapping** dialog where you pick:
  - Bin
  - Material
  - Stock/QTY
  - (optional) Capacity
  - (optional) Description

**Capacity from the export is ignored** anyway once you set row capacities.

---

## Running the script (Python)

### Requirements
- Python 3.10+ recommended
- Packages: `pandas`, `openpyxl`, `lxml`, `pyinstaller`

Install:
```powershell
python -m pip install --upgrade pip
python -m pip install pandas openpyxl lxml pyinstaller
```

Run:
```powershell
python .\\consolidator_gui.py
```

---

## Building a USB-ready Windows EXE (recommended)

From a clean folder (example `C:\\Consolidator`):

```powershell
mkdir C:\\Consolidator -Force
cd C:\\Consolidator

python -m venv .venv
.\\.venv\\Scripts\\Activate.ps1

[ASSISTANT]
```markdown
# Consolidator (Line-Clearance Bin Optimizer)

Windows desktop tool that reads a SAP warehouse “snapshot” export and generates a **move list** to **clear bins near the line** by moving stock into farther bins where space exists.

This build uses **row-based capacity overrides** because SAP-exported bin capacity is not reliable for your floor layout.

---

## What the program asks for

1) **Input file**: a SAP export (snapshot) in one of these formats:
- **Excel**: `.xlsx` / `.xls`
- **HTML**: `.htm` / `.html` (SAP “Email/HTML” style export)
- **XML**: `.xml` (SpreadsheetML variants and InventoryExport-style XML)

2) **Threshold** (number):
- Bins with **BinNum >= threshold** are treated as **SOURCES** (stock you want to pull OUT).
- Bins with **BinNum < threshold** are treated as **TARGETS** (bins you want to fill, keeping them near-line).

3) **Row Capacity Overrides** (required):
- The app detects all **Rows** in the file (A, B, C, …, AA, etc.)
- You must choose a capacity **2–45** for **each Row**.
- There are **no defaults**.
- The report **will not run** until every detected Row has a capacity selected.

---

## How it decides moves (current workflow)

For each **Material**:
- **Targets** = bins with `BinNum < threshold` and `Qty < Capacity`
- **Sources** = bins with `BinNum >= threshold` and `Qty > 0`
- It moves stock from **higher BinNum → lower BinNum** until targets are full or sources are empty.

Output is a plain-text report listing:
- Material
- FromBin → ToBin
- Quantity
- Description (if present in export)

---

## Supported file quirks

The parser is designed to survive SAP export differences:
- If column headers differ, it tries **auto-detection** by name and by content.
- If it still can’t tell which column is which, it opens a **column mapping** dialog where you pick:
  - Bin
  - Material
  - Stock/QTY
  - (optional) Capacity
  - (optional) Description

**Capacity from the export is ignored** once you set row capacities.

---

## Running the script (Python)

### Requirements
- Python 3.10+ recommended
- Packages: `pandas`, `openpyxl`, `lxml`, `pyinstaller`

Install:
```powershell
python -m pip install --upgrade pip
python -m pip install pandas openpyxl lxml pyinstaller
```

Run:
```powershell
python .\consolidator_gui.py
```

---

## Building a USB-ready Windows EXE

From a clean folder (example `C:\Consolidator`):

```powershell
mkdir C:\Consolidator -Force
cd C:\Consolidator

python -m venv .venv
.\.venv\Scripts\Activate.ps1

python -m pip install --upgrade pip
python -m pip install pandas openpyxl lxml pyinstaller
```

Put your script in this folder as:
- `consolidator_gui.py`

Build:
```powershell
python -m PyInstaller --onefile --windowed --name Consolidator --collect-all pandas --collect-all lxml --collect-all openpyxl .\consolidator_gui.py
```

Your EXE will be:
- `C:\Consolidator\dist\Consolidator.exe`

Copy that EXE to your USB.

**Work laptop note:** if Windows blocks EXEs from USB, copy it to `C:\temp\Consolidator.exe` before running. If needed: right-click → Properties → **Unblock**.

---

## Output / Saving

- The generated report appears in the right panel.
- Click **Save Report** to write it to a `.txt` file you choose.

---

## Troubleshooting

### “Import openpyxl failed…”
Cause: your environment/EXE doesn’t include `openpyxl`.

Fix (script):
```powershell
python -m pip install openpyxl
```

Fix (EXE):
1) Install `openpyxl` in the build venv  
2) Rebuild using `--collect-all openpyxl` (see build command above)

### “PowerShell does not load commands from current location”
Use:
```powershell
python .\consolidator_gui.py
```
not just `consolidator_gui.py`.

### Mapping failed / columns not found
That export layout is different. Use the **column mapping dialog** and select the correct columns (Bin/Material/Stock). Then generate again.

### Report won’t run
You haven’t set a capacity for every detected Row in the left panel. Pick **2–45** for all rows listed.

### Consolidator – Quick User Readme (how to run it)

#### 1) Export the snapshot from SAP
1. Go to **LS24** (bin status) or your **Bin Status Report**.
2. Run the report so you see the bin list on screen.
3. Use the menu path:  
   **Bin Status Rpt → File → Spreadsheet**  
4. Save it to your **Downloads** folder as an **.XLSX**.

> If SAP tries to save as HTML or some other format, you changed the default earlier. You’ll need to switch the format back to XLSX when it prompts (or use the program’s HTML option if you saved as .htm).

---

#### 2) Open Consolidator
1. Plug in your USB (if you’re running it from USB).
2. Double-click **Consolidator.exe**.

> If Windows blocks it from USB: copy it to `C:\temp\Consolidator.exe` and run it from there.

---

#### 3) Load the export
1. Click **Browse**
2. Go to: **Downloads**
3. Select your **.XLSX** export
4. Click **Open**

---

#### 4) Set the Threshold
- The **Threshold** decides what bins are “far” vs “near”:
  - **BinNum >= Threshold** = **sources** (bins you want emptied)
  - **BinNum < Threshold** = **targets** (bins you want filled)

Set it to whatever cutoff you use for “near the line.”

---

#### 5) Set Row Capacities (required)
On the left side you’ll see a list like:
- Row A
- Row B
- Row C
- etc.

For **each row**, pick a capacity from **2 to 45**.

**No capacity = no report.**  
If even one row is blank, it won’t generate moves.

*(This is because SAP’s capacity numbers are wrong, so the tool uses your row values instead.)*

---

#### 6) Generate the move list
1. Click **Generate Report**
2. The right panel will populate with move instructions like:  
   `MOVE X of Material: FromBin -> ToBin`

If it says **no moves found**, it means either:
- the “far” bins are already empty, or
- the “near” bins are already full (based on the row capacities you set)

---

#### 7) Save the report
1. Click **Save Report**
2. Save it as a `.txt` file (ex: `LineClearance_Moves.txt`)

---

### If you get a “column mapping” popup
Sometimes SAP exports with weird headers. If the tool can’t auto-detect columns, it will ask you to choose:
- Bin column
- Material column
- Stock/QTY column  
(Description/Capacity are optional)

Pick the correct ones and continue.

---

### Common problems
**“Import openpyxl failed…”**  
Your EXE was built without Excel support. Rebuild with `openpyxl` included.

**EXE blocked from USB**  
Copy it to `C:\temp` and run it locally.

---

If you want, tell me your exact SAP screen name/version (LS24 layout varies) and I’ll rewrite the export steps with the exact menu labels you see.
